  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d34c114f-6b61-49c3-b105-c41a8140fbfb'
      });

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText5486246613217257787" style="display:none">A publishing event: Bestselling author Ken Liu selects his award-winning science fiction and fantasy tales for a groundbreaking collection—including a brand-new piece exclusive to this volume.<br /><br />With his debut novel, <i>The Grace of Kings</i>, taking the literary world by storm, Ken Liu now shares his finest short fiction in <i>The Paper Menagerie</i>. This mesmerizing collection features all of Ken’s award-winning and award-finalist stories, including: “The Man Who Ended History: A Documentary” (Finalist for the Hugo, Nebula, and Theodore Sturgeon Awards), “Mono No Aware” (Hugo Award winner), “The Waves” (Nebula Award finalist), “The Bookmaking Habits of Select Species” (Nebula and Sturgeon award finalists), “All the Flavors” (Nebula award finalist), “The Litigation Master and the Monkey King” (Nebula Award finalist), and the most awarded story in the genre’s history, “The Paper Menagerie” (The only story to win the Hugo, Nebula, and World Fantasy awards).<br /><br />A must-have for every science fiction and fantasy fan, this beautiful book is an anthology to savor.</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/966445-can-someone-please-tell-me-why-ken-liu-is">Can someone please tell me why Ken Liu is often categorized as young adult? While I have nothing against YA, this book seems far from it.</a>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Because people believe that accessible writing isn't for adults.<br/><br/>I often see this problem with fantasy and sci fi being considered for young readers si<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Because people believe that accessible writing isn't for adults.<br /><br />I often see this problem with fantasy and sci fi being considered for young readers simply because it is genre fiction. It's a common supposition that's unfair to most authors categorized that way.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_2015371117" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2015371117" />
    <a title="Michael Finocchiaro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48483884-michael-finocchiaro"><img alt="Michael Finocchiaro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576692048p2/48483884.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2015371117?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Finocchiaro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Finocchiaro" href="/user/show/48483884-michael-finocchiaro">Michael Finocchiaro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48483884-michael-finocchiaro?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48483884-michael-finocchiaro?shelf=american-21st-c">american-21st-c</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48483884-michael-finocchiaro?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48483884-michael-finocchiaro?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2015371117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12187564779138921106">Absolutely stunning collection of short stories which teach and entertain in equal measure. Ken Liu has an incredible imagination and these stories are all so different and yet all so amazing. I, like many others, come to Ken Liu after his superb translations of Cixin Liu's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20518872.The_Three_Body_Problem__Remembrance_of_Earth_s_Past__1_' title='The Three-Body Problem (Remembrance of Earth’s Past #1) by Liu Cixin' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Three-Body Problem</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25451264.Death_s_End__Remembrance_of_Earth_s_Past__3_' title='Death's End (Remembrance of Earth’s Past #3) by Liu Cixin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Death's End</a> and I can see that he was the perfect choice because his love of language and culture echoes that of Cixin Liu in many, many ways. I also saw some commonality in some of their sci fi ide</span>
  <span id="freeText12187564779138921106" style="display:none">Absolutely stunning collection of short stories which teach and entertain in equal measure. Ken Liu has an incredible imagination and these stories are all so different and yet all so amazing. I, like many others, come to Ken Liu after his superb translations of Cixin Liu's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20518872.The_Three_Body_Problem__Remembrance_of_Earth_s_Past__1_" title="The Three-Body Problem (Remembrance of Earth’s Past #1) by Liu Cixin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Three-Body Problem</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25451264.Death_s_End__Remembrance_of_Earth_s_Past__3_" title="Death's End (Remembrance of Earth’s Past #3) by Liu Cixin" rel="nofollow noopener">Death's End</a> and I can see that he was the perfect choice because his love of language and culture echoes that of Cixin Liu in many, many ways. I also saw some commonality in some of their sci fi ideas. But, it is the realistic depiction of his characters and the innate poetry of the prose that helped me plunge into each story. I loved each one and found that each asked fundamental questions:<br /><br />The Bookmaking Habits of Select Species - this one reminded me a lot of Italo Calvino. Questions asked: What is literature? How is it transmitted and interpreted?<br />State Change - fantastic compact story with lovely vignettes about TS Elliott, Joan of Arc, etc. Questions asked: What is the soul? What is our capacity for change?<br />Perfect Match - loved the reference to Vivaldi's Violin Concerto in C Minor, haunting dystopia where Google and Amazon Alexa rule the world. Questions asked: What is free choice? How much are we willing to compromise on privacy before our lives become completely passive?<br />Good Hunting - love story with magic, steampunk, transformation. Questions asked: How big a cultural price are we willing to pay for technological progress? <br />The Literomancer - gorgeous, painful, amazing. Love the idea of word magic, poetic. Questions asked: How does language, our choice of works, express identity? <br />Simulacrum - spooky. Questions asked: Where do we draw the line in reality between the real and the simulated? Once love is objectified, is it still love?<br />The Regular - great murder mystery - idea of emotion suppressor is great, but open wifi is terrifying. Are emotions an impediment or a tool in a critical situation? Can we be redeemed?<br />The Paper Menagerie - beautiful and magical story. What is memory? How do we see keep a sense of wonder as we grow older? Does magic exist?<br />An Advanced Reader’s Picture Book of Comparative Cognition (previously unpublished) - similar to first story but on communication, chocolate analogy. What is thought? How do we learn? Can electric sheep dream?<br />The Waves - solar sails, greek mythology, russian doll stort stacking, seafoam was a beautiful image. Would immortality be a paradise or a hell? Is death a release or an end? Where is the boundary between machine and consciousness?<br />Mono no aware - lovely - go and poetry and web of others eyes, kitten's tongue. How do we love? How do we express love?<br />All the Flavors - western, Idaho City fire 1865 - awesome story about Chinese Immigrants for the railroad that end up mining and classic Chinese myths. How do we set aside preconceived ideas and open up to other cultures? Must the meeting of two disparate cultures always end in tears and bloodshed, or can it be harmonious?<br />A Brief History of the Trans-Pacific Tunnel - sci fi dystopia racism formosan. Can one redeem oneself from the unforgivable? What are the limits to human adaptability?<br />The Litigation Master and the Monkey King - great story from Qinglong dynasty. How do we liberate history from willful forgetfulness? What is a hero?<br />The Man Who Ended History: A Documentary -devastating but amazing. <br />See this <a href="http://time.com/4854718/quantum-entanglement-teleport-space/" rel="nofollow noopener">article</a> to see that the Chinese are making swift progress with quantum entanglement in our era already. As for the atrocities discussed (Nanjing Massacre and especially Unit 731 in Pingfang, China) and the debate around their historicity and the guilt of the perpetrators, this is all very, very real. Note that the US is not innocent here either:<br />"MacArthur struck a deal with Japanese informants—he secretly granted immunity to the physicians of Unit 731, including their leader, in exchange for providing America, but not the other wartime allies, with their research on biological warfare and data from human experimentation."<br />From Wikipedia article quoting Unit 731 Testimony by Hal Gold (2011)<br />Questions asked: What are the relative values to subjective and objective perception? What boundaries define history and ownership of history? How do we deal with acts of extreme depravity without becoming deranged or depraved ourselves? Does every act of preservation necessary involve and act of destruction? How do we assign guilt when the victims are dead, their names and remains vaporized and the perpetrators neatly all dead? How do we validate history? What is truth? What is justice? Yeah, this one opens up a LOT of questions for the reader!<br /><br />I hope that wasn't too hard to read. Some things I infer about Ken Liu from these stories that may or may not be true:<br />1/ he has lived in New England and Idaho<br />2/ he is an incredible linguist with fluency in at least English, Chinese and Japanese<br />3/ he is extremely well-read<br />4/ his major social concerns are around cultural preservation, the indelible value of memory, the persistence of love<br />5/ it would be absolutely fascinating to have a conversation with him over beers, whiskey or wine :-)<br /><br />Read these stories and be transported to different times and different worlds. Question everything. Lastly remember Socrates: The unexamined life is not worth living.<br /><br />Nota bene: I listened to this on Amazon Audible and found the dual narrators great - especially in pronouncing the Chinese names. But honestly, this is a book that I have purchased on paper because I want to see if the ideogram analysis he performs in The Literomancer and All the Flavors is illustrated with the Chinese characters he mentions. I have passed it to a friend already and she loves it and can't put it down!<br />Highly recommended summer reading!!<br /><br />Fino's Cixin Liu and other Chinese SciFi and Fantasy Reviews<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2001737886?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Three Body Problem</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2001737901?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dark Forest</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2001737924?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Death's End</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2160451709?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wandering Earth</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3025780859?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Supernova Era"</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3058287023?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Ball Lightning</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2256217008?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Redemption of Time (Fan Fiction approved by Cixin Liu)</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2107808726?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Invisible Planets (Short Story Anthology)</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2015371117?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Paper Menagerie and Other Stories</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2015371116?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Grace of Kings</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2015371198?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wall of Storms</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12187564779138921106" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2174621319" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2174621319" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2174621319?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Petrik by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/7224501-katherine">Katherine</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59458347-petrik?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2174621319" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11573677037260801727"><i>I have a Booktube channel now! Subscribe here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.youtube.com/petrikleo'>https://www.youtube.com/petrikleo</a></i><br/><br/><b>4.5/5 stars<br/><br/><i>The Paper Menagerie and Other Stories</i> is an intimately powerful and beautiful collection of stories that encompassed some of the most relatable themes to our society, and some stories contained in this collection felt personal and evocative to me.<br/><br/><i><blockquote>“Every act of communication is a miracle of translation.”</blockquote></i></b><br/><br/>Excluding translation works, this collection marked my first experience of reading Ken Liu’s original sto</span>
  <span id="freeText11573677037260801727" style="display:none"><i>I have a Booktube channel now! Subscribe here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/petrikleo">https://www.youtube.com/petrikleo</a></i><br /><br /><b>4.5/5 stars<br /><br /><i>The Paper Menagerie and Other Stories</i> is an intimately powerful and beautiful collection of stories that encompassed some of the most relatable themes to our society, and some stories contained in this collection felt personal and evocative to me.<br /><br /><i><blockquote>“Every act of communication is a miracle of translation.”</blockquote></i></b><br /><br />Excluding translation works, this collection marked my first experience of reading Ken Liu’s original stories. Ken Liu did a fantastic job on translating <i>The Three-Body Problem</i> and <i>Death’s End</i>, the first and third book in <i>The Remembrance of Earth’s Past</i> trilogy by Cixin Liu. Because of this, immediately after I finished reading <i>The Remembrance of Earth’s Past</i> trilogy by Cixin Liu, I knew that I must also read Ken Liu’s original stories. The result totally exceeded my expectations. Ken Liu truly has a way with words; the Asian-inspired tales he implemented were brilliant, and he weaved these short stories and transformed them into an emotionally impactful reading experience. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“We are defined by the places we hold in the web of others’ lives.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />One of the main topics featured heavily in this collection is the struggle of adapting or coping with Eastern and Western culture; differences in culture, language, and racial prejudice are reoccurring themes. Full disclosure that English is my third language. I’m a Chinese born and raised in Indonesia, and I grew up learning about all three Chinese, Indonesian, and Western cultures and languages due to my upbringing, environment, and education. This is the most pivotal reason why most of the short stories here resonated with me. I understand how difficult it can be to learn and adapt to different cultures and languages, especially on an everyday basis; I’m still learning up to this day, and I will always continue to do so. The majority of my friends and followers on Goodreads, as far as I know, are not Asian, but even if you’re not, this collection is still a must-read if you’re looking for amazing fictions that will also help you understand more about Asian history, way of life, superstition, and struggles.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Our lives are ruled by these small, seemingly ordinary moments that turn out to have improbably large effects.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />As you can probably guess from the books I’ve reviewed, I’m generally not a fan of short stories or novellas; more often than not, they’re too short to have a lasting impression on me. However, this collection is exceptional. Almost all of the stories exhibited in this collection were wonderfully well-written. They’re memorable, philosophical, introspective, fascinating, and some of them were extraordinarily emotional. I’m thoroughly amazed by the versatility of Liu’s storytelling. Whether it’s fantasy, sci-fi, magical realism, noir thriller, or historical fiction, <i>The Paper Menagerie and Other Stories</i> has them all. If you’re a fan of speculative fiction, I honestly don’t see how most of these stories won’t work for you. I’m not kidding, out of fifteen stories included in this collection, only two of them didn’t click with me. As for the rest? I either liked them or absolutely loved them. Due to the short length of the majority of the stories contained here, I won’t be doing any review on them. I do, however, want to do a short review for two of my utmost favorite short stories in this collection: <i>The Paper Menagerie</i> and <i>The Man Who Ended History: A Documentary.</i><br /><br /><b>
  <u>
    <i>The Paper Menagerie</i>
  </u>
</b><br /><br /><i>The Paper Menagerie</i> is purely magical. For those of you who don’t know, <i>The Paper Menagerie</i> was the only work of fiction to ever win all Hugo, Nebula, and World Fantasy awards within a single year. It is with many great reasons, validity, and recognitions that this collection is titled <i>The Paper Menagerie and Other Stories</i>; the titular story is simply a scintillating piece of literature. 15 pages long, just within 15 pages, Ken Liu has created something that’s truly emotional, important, and mesmerizing. The topics of empathy, mother’s love for their child, and the acceptance of our own race embedded in this short story undeniably tugged at my heartstrings. <i>The Paper Menagerie</i> is a brilliantly imaginative, poignant, and magnificently written short story that almost made me cry within 15 pages. This is, hands down, the best short stories I’ve ever read, and I don’t think I will ever find a better short story than this in my life. I’d give this masterwork a 6/5 stars rating if I could.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>
    <i>The Man Who Ended History: A Documentary</i>
  </u>
</b><br /><br /><i>The Man Who Ended History: A Documentary</i> tells the brutal story of Unit 731—lethal human experimentation that’s responsible for some of the vilest and notorious crimes enacted by the Japanese during the Second Sino-Japanese War. It’s dark, violent, terrifying, depressing, and it made many grimdark novels tame in comparison. The craziest part about this, though, is the fact that the Unit 731 incident is real; this isn’t fictional, Unit 731 is a part of humanity’s history. The world knows about the Nazi and Auschwitz concentration camp, but it’s shocking to me that many people—Asian or not—have never heard about this atrocious incident. <b>If you’re reading this review and you’ve never heard of Unit 731 or the Second Sino-Japanese War, I hope you’ll find the time to do some research on them.</b> These incidents will most likely make you feel grateful for the life you have now. <i>The Man Who Ended History: A Documentary</i> is one of the most powerful novellas I’ve ever read, and it is truly the most fitting story to close this superb collection.<br /><br />I’ve said all I needed to say; you have to experience this book for yourself. Suffice to say that I’ve arrived at the conclusion that I would be doing myself an immense injustice if I don’t read more of Ken Liu’s works, especially <i>The Dandelion Dynasty</i> series, which sounds like everything I’m looking for in epic fantasy. Intelligently crafted, thought-provoking, and emotionally devastating, I highly recommend <i>The Paper Menagerie and Other Stories</i> collection to every reader of speculative fiction. It is easily one of the finest collection of stories I’ve ever read so far.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“And yet, whatever has been lost in translation in the long journey of my thoughts through the maze of civilization to your mind, I think you do understand me, and you think you do understand me. Our minds managed to touch, if but briefly and imperfectly.<br /><br />Does that thought not make the universe seem just a bit kinder, a bit brighter, a bit warmer and more human?<br /><br />We live for such miracles.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br /><b>You can order the book from: <u><a href="https://www.amazon.co.uk/Paper-Menagerie-Ken-Liu/dp/1784975699/ref=sr_1_1?dchild=1&amp;keywords=the+paper+menagerie&amp;qid=1603434036&amp;sr=8-1" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon UK</a></u> | <u><a href="https://www.amazon.com/Paper-Menagerie-Other-Stories/dp/1481442546/ref=tmm_hrd_swatch_0?_encoding=UTF8&amp;qid=1603433646&amp;sr=8-" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon US</a></u> | <u><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/book/9781481424363/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository (Free shipping)</a></u> | <u><a href="https://bookshop.org/a/1165/9781481424363" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookshop (Support Local Bookstores!)</a></u></b><br /><br /><b>You can find <u><a href="http://novelnotions.net/2020/10/23/book-review-the-paper-menagerie-and-other-stories-by-ken-liu-2/" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></u> and the rest of my reviews at <u><a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a></u></b><br /><br /><i>Special thanks to my Patrons on <b><u><a href="https://www.patreon.com/petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Patreon</a></u></b> for giving me extra support towards my passion for reading and reviewing!<br /><br />My Patrons: Alfred, Alya, Annabeth, Blaise, Devin, Diana, Edward, Hamad, Helen, Jimmy Nutts, Joie, Michelle, Mike, Miracle, Nicholas, Zoe.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11573677037260801727" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1710199737" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1710199737" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1710199737?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1710199737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10450423188594358030">A beautifully written, powerful anthology of first-rate speculative fiction stories.<br/><br/>Ken Liu is an impressive guy, besides writing he is also a lawyer and a programmer. Many readers first read his translation of Liu Cixin’s Hugo award winning novel <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20518872.The_Three_Body_Problem__Remembrance_of_Earth_s_Past__1_' title='The Three-Body Problem (Remembrance of Earth’s Past #1) by Liu Cixin' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Three-Body Problem</a>. I read his 2014 Tor.com short work <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20653250.Reborn__The_Anderson_Project___1_' title='Reborn (The Anderson Project, #1) by Ken Liu' rel='nofollow noopener'>Reborn</a> and so had a good idea he can produce a gem on his own.<br/><br/>Building on ubiquitous themes of Asian-American cultural pluralities and Chinese myth and legend, Liu does an impressive job creati</span>
  <span id="freeText10450423188594358030" style="display:none">A beautifully written, powerful anthology of first-rate speculative fiction stories.<br><br>Ken Liu is an impressive guy, besides writing he is also a lawyer and a programmer. Many readers first read his translation of Liu Cixin’s Hugo award winning novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20518872.The_Three_Body_Problem__Remembrance_of_Earth_s_Past__1_" title="The Three-Body Problem (Remembrance of Earth’s Past #1) by Liu Cixin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Three-Body Problem</a>. I read his 2014 Tor.com short work <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20653250.Reborn__The_Anderson_Project___1_" title="Reborn (The Anderson Project, #1) by Ken Liu" rel="nofollow noopener">Reborn</a> and so had a good idea he can produce a gem on his own.<br><br>Building on ubiquitous themes of Asian-American cultural pluralities and Chinese myth and legend, Liu does an impressive job creating a continuing and pervasive sense of inventiveness. These fifteen stories, some sketches and others novella sized range from cool sci-fi to wildly imaginative fantasy and everything in between.<br><br>“State Change” features a girl whose soul was an ice cube. One of my favorites was “The Perfect Match" which describes a futuristic Siri type all inclusive app called Sintillian that takes surveillance to a whole new level and Liu throws in some interesting twists.<br><br>“Good Hunting” is a smooth blend of Asian myth and steampunk.<br><br>“The Literomancer” is a heartbreaking story that shows an old man tortured and a red headed Texan girl in a morality play on Cold War policies.<br><br>Another of my favorites was “The Regular", a novella length cyborg murder mystery.<br><br>“The Paper Menagerie” was the story that got all the press and some awards, but it was not my favorite by far. A bittersweet fantasy about generational and cultural chasms.<br><br>“An Advanced Reader’s Picture Book of Comparative Cognition” (previously unpublished) is a very Poul Anderson kind of story, reminiscent especially of Anderson’s 1970 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/240617.Tau_Zero" title="Tau Zero by Poul Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Tau Zero</a>. “The Waves” is another Poul Anderson inspired work, this one like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/338327.The_Boat_of_a_Million_Years" title="The Boat of a Million Years by Poul Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Boat of a Million Years</a>. “Mono no aware” is a Bradburyesque tale of space.<br><br>“All the Flavors” is a western from the perspective of a little girl. My favorite TV show of all time is Kung Fu, and the Chinese characters in this western setting reminded me pleasingly of the show.<br><br>“A Brief History of the Trans-Pacific Tunnel” was a very Heinleinesque, optimistic alternate history story about – what else?<br><br>“The Litigation Master and the Monkey King" – fantastic and fun, litigators should always be in the protagonist role. Liu the juris doctor shows his stripes.<br><br>Liu saved his best and most powerful for the last. “The Man Who Ended History: A Documentary” Stories of Nazi atrocities are well known in the west but Liu reminds us about horrific injustices committed by the Japanese. Using some ingenious time travel ideas, Liu revisits the Japanese occupation of Manchuria and paints a brutal portrait of inhumanity. I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/767171.The_Rise_and_Fall_of_the_Third_Reich_A_History_of_Nazi_Germany" title="The Rise and Fall of the Third Reich A History of Nazi Germany by William L. Shirer" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rise and Fall of the Third Reich: A History of Nazi Germany</a> a few years ago and it took months to gear myself up for the task and then months afterwards to recover. There is only so much horror the mind can take. I will someday read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/95784.The_Rape_of_Nanking" title="The Rape of Nanking by Iris Chang" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rape of Nanking</a> that documents this same occupation, but reading Liu’s story has set this reading back further.<br><br>For readers of modern speculative fiction, this is a must read.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1560253368i/27650821._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="266" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="10450423188594358030" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1391151137" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1391151137" />
    <a title="Matthew Quann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22699228-matthew-quann"><img alt="Matthew Quann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528393487p2/22699228.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1391151137?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew Quann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew Quann" href="/user/show/22699228-matthew-quann">Matthew Quann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22699228-matthew-quann?shelf=collaborative-review">collaborative-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22699228-matthew-quann?shelf=short-story-collections">short-story-collections</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22699228-matthew-quann?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22699228-matthew-quann?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22699228-matthew-quann?shelf=sff-award-winners">sff-award-winners</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22699228-matthew-quann?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1391151137" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12948736990489863235"><b>A review of all short stories in this collection featuring my parents!</b><br/><br/>Herein contains a review unlike any other I’ve done! I get home so infrequently that I drummed up the idea of involving my parents in some of my reading. My parents enjoy the odd book, but aren’t what I would describe as avid readers. So I proposed that I would read them a story a night (for 15 nights) from acclaimed sci-fi and fantasy author Ken Liu’s <i>The Paper Menagerie</i>. <br/><br/>All they knew about the book prior to the reading was </span>
  <span id="freeText12948736990489863235" style="display:none"><b>A review of all short stories in this collection featuring my parents!</b><br /><br />Herein contains a review unlike any other I’ve done! I get home so infrequently that I drummed up the idea of involving my parents in some of my reading. My parents enjoy the odd book, but aren’t what I would describe as avid readers. So I proposed that I would read them a story a night (for 15 nights) from acclaimed sci-fi and fantasy author Ken Liu’s <i>The Paper Menagerie</i>. <br /><br />All they knew about the book prior to the reading was that it was going to be fantastical. They had no idea that Liu’s eponymous story won the Hugo, Nebula, and World Fantasy Award all in the same year nor, I hazard, would they have cared. Then, following the reading, I asked them two questions: <br /><br />1) Did you like the story?<br />2) What did or didn’t you like?<br /><br />What follows are my parents’ thoughts (collected interview style post-read) and mine in brief. I’ve done my best to capture my parents’ voices and reactions as accurately as possible, though I’ve truncated some thoughts where appropriate. These stories were read between a brief summer working holiday and the Christmas break. Enjoy!<br /><br /><b>NOTE: my (brief) overall review is at the very end if you're just looking for my thoughts!</b><br /><br /><i>1.The Bookmaking Habits of Select Species</i><br /><br /><b>Momma Q</b>: No (emphatically)! <br />I think the dude that wrote it was on acid or something. People that read by smelling? *inquisitive look* Who has thoughts like that? Those can’t be drug-free thoughts, he couldn’t have not been on drugs. <br /><br /><b>Dad Q</b>: At times I did like it!<br />“WTF?”Can I start with that? Am I allowed to say WTF? I enjoyed that people read through science, smells, traveling through stars. I think it is about all the different ways that stories can be told and the way they change like when the Romans told stories compared to someone who does science writing. <br /><br /><b>Matt</b>: Yeah, I dug this.<br />As I was reading this, I kept thinking that my parents had to be suffering through it, but I trudged on. Liu’s fantastical creatures have me excited for the rest of the stories and it seems like a pretty smooth move to start off a short story collection with a story about books and stories. I enjoyed my parents’ reactions and I really liked my dad’s interpretation. I’m excited to see what tomorrow’s story brings. <br /><br /><i>2. State Change</i><br /><br /><b>Momma Q</b>: I liked it.<br />I liked the fact that it ended up nice. Everyone ended up happy and not dead. I like the concept that everyone has a different object as a soul. I wonder what mine is?<br /><br /><b>Dad Q</b>: Yes, I liked it.<br />She lived her life as a piece of ice, and it is cool that she was so closed off that people didn’t even know the colour of her eyes. I liked that even though she was a closed off person, she enjoyed reading about other peoples lives. Also, a threesome. <br /><br /><b>Matt</b>: Oh yeah, big win!<br />I thought this story was peculiar, but smart, well realized, and the perfect example of sci-fi done right. The story had a lot of heart to it and provided a beautiful metaphor for social isolation and how different personalities interact. This story was also radically different from the first, so I hope that the next brings as much surprise!<br /><br /><i>3.Perfect Match</i><br /><br /><b>Momma Q</b>: I liked it.<br />The only thing is that it is a story that has been told over and over again. <br /><br /><b>Dad Q</b>: I really liked it.<br />I feel like that’s what we’re living right now with our cellphones. Our cellphones have passwords, doctor appointments, phone numbers; it is the world we’re living in. <br /><br /><b>Matt</b> I liked it too!<br />I’ll have to side with mom on this one and agree that this is a type of story we see a lot of these days. With that said, this was another well-done, smart sci-fi story. I get the feeling after reading this one that it could be mined for a Hollywood adaptation.<br /><br /><i>4. Good Hunting</i><br /><br /><b>Momma Q</b>: I did like it.<br />I didn’t know what was going to happen. I really liked how I didn’t have any idea where the story would go. I found it very original. <br /><br /><b>Dad Q</b>: Yes, I liked it.<br />I enjoyed that the story was about adapting to changes. It wasn’t a typical love story, but I liked how it was about the two characters adapting together. <br /><br />[SIDELINE: Mom and Dad debated whether or not this was a story about romantic love, or a different kind of love.]<br /><br /><b>Matt</b> That was awesome!<br />This was such an imaginative story and an excellent blend of the fantastical with a peculiar steampunk world. It was really difficult to know where the story was going, and I admit to being genuinely surprised by the ending. Writing was, again, on point. <br /><br /><i>5. The Literomancer</i><br /><br /><b>Momma Q</b>: I liked it.<br />I don’t know much about Chinese history during the cold war, or that part of the world, really. I like the concept of ‘do unto others.’ The torture scene was awful.<br /><br /><b>Dad Q</b>: I liked it.<br />It was a bit all over the place, but it was a good representation of even after a war is over, it has changes. It tears families apart and changes people on both sides. I feel like I learned some life lessons about people doing good.<br /><br /><b>Matt</b>: I’m into it.<br />But man, was that ever unexpectedly heavy. It really threw me for a loop to move from the really unique fantasy/sci-fi into this highly serious historical account of the atrocities committed by American spies against the Chinese populace. The mood was dour after this reading, and rightly so. I’m very impressed with Mr. Liu. <br /><br /><i>6. Simulacrum</i><br /><br /><b>Momma Q</b>: I didn’t love it, that’s for sure.<br />I think that everybody should be forgiven and I think it is a terrible tragedy when people can’t forgive one another. <br /><br /><b>Dad Q</b>: I didn’t like it.<br />It felt like one of those “Made-in-Canada” movies. The man was stuck in a life that was fake instead of interacting with the real one. <br /><br /><b>Matt</b> Hey, I thought it was good!<br />My parents were, obviously, not that into this one; however, I thought it was poignant. It was so inarguably sad, but the message was a good one: forgive your loved ones. I mean, 10 pages of these poor people stuck in a limbo of dysfunction with an underlying sci-fi concept was, again, a great display of Liu’s skills. <br /><br /><i>7.The Regular</i><br /><br /><b>Momma Q</b>: I didn’t understand it, I guess I didn’t like it.<br />I had a hard time following it. I fell asleep a bit during the start. I just don’t understand it, that’s all.<br /><br /><b>Dad Q</b>: Liked it very much.<br />A great story. The detective’s trauma motivated her to use the regulator to watch her emotions, but her emotions also draw her in to help the victim’s mother. I think story about forgiveness and making amends. I like that all the characters came together through their loss. <br /><br /><b>Matt</b> This was awesome!<br />I wasn’t expecting a murder mystery in this collection, but boy, that was great stuff! I often find thrillers to be not thrilling enough, or so fixed on thrills that they just end up being a slight twist on a story you’ve read before. This was smart, the use of sci-fi was original, and there was a strong emotional core to this story. This keeps on being a winner.<br /><br /><i>8. The Paper Menagerie</i><br /><br /><b>Momma Q</b>: I thought it was really nice.<br />I think it is what happens to us as parents. We’re not in style, or not the prettiest. But if you’re lucky, you get to grow up and find out your parents love you. I think it is a beautiful story.<br /><br /><b>Dad Q</b>: I liked it.<br />I think the young fella allowed peer pressure to influence him. You never know a person until you walk a mile in their shoes, and so he never got to know his mother until after she was gone. <br /><br /><b>Matt</b> Loved it.<br />Man, this one almost had me tearing up during the reading! Such a touching story that brings home the fraught relationships we can have with our parents and the difficulties we can have in understanding one another. Also, I love learning about Chinese history and Chinese immigrant stories through Liu’s gorgeous writing. <br /><br /><i>9.An Advanced Readers’ Picture Book of Comparative Cognition</i><br /><br /><b>Momma Q</b>: No, I didn’t like it.<br />I found it so complicated. I don’t know what the point was of telling us all of those science-y things if not just to show off that he knows science-y things. <br /><br /><b>Dad Q</b>: I didn’t like it.<br />WTF! The storyline, once you start getting into chemicals, distances between planets, and all that stuff, you lose me. It’s hard to follow a storyline like that, I don’t care about that stuff. I flatlined during this story.<br /><br /><b>Matt</b> Man, my parents are wack. This was great.<br />Okay, a bit of an explanation. These are fairy tales about extraterrestrial races who are each supposed to embody one of the cardinal sciences. These stories are also interspersed with the story of a mother who left her family for the stars. I think it would be difficult to enjoy without a strong science background, but I just fawned over it. <br /><br /><i>10. The Waves</i><br /><br /><b>Momma Q</b>: I liked it.<br />I thought it was awful sad though, everyone was alone. <br /><br /><b>Dad Q</b>: I liked it.<br />I love the stories about the gods and goddesses, the whole alien thing was cool too. <br /><br /><b>Matt</b> I just thought it was okay.<br />The story’s take on religion and creation was neat, but this was the story that I thought had the least heart. Still, this is a lot better than some sci-fi I’ve read. <br /><br /><i>11. Mono No Aware</i><br /><br /><b>Momma Q</b>: I liked it (though she is crying).<br />I found it pretty sad. It’s kind of like Jesus isn’t it? <br /><br /><b>Dad Q</b>: I liked it (not crying).<br />A few times I found the story a bit scattered, I wasn’t sure when it was set. I liked that the character followed the path that was laid out for him and wasn’t afraid.<br /><br /><b>Matt</b> I liked it (also, not crying)<br />A touching story, so I can totally understand why mom put on the waterworks. Once again, this is a space-faring story, but I loved the Japanese influence. I also, completely ignorant of real rocket science, feel that his science fiction is plausible.<br /><br /><i>12. All The Flavors</i><br /><br /><b>Matt</b>: I liked it!<br />This was one of the long ones (~100 pages), so I just read this one on my own. What surprises me most about this collection is that I expected a straight SF/F set of stories, but I ended up getting a lot of historical fiction. <i>All the Flavors</i> is a tale about Chinese immigrants in the US with a Western setting. Liu’s got a talent for exposing relatively unknown historical facts with heartfelt stories. This one is no different!<br /><br /><i>13.A Brief History of The Trans-Pacific Tunnel</i><br /><br /><b>Momma Q</b>: I liked the story.<br />I liked that the main character was able to find love and talk about his trauma.<br /><br /><b>Dad Q</b>: I liked it.<br />I think it was about how we don’t tell stories until we find someone we can trust. <br /><br /><b>Matt</b> I liked it.<br />I liked the alternate history take. Was this supposed to be a realistic take on “digging a tunnel to China?” I certainly thought so. I also like the way Liu includes (fictional) historical documents within his short stories. <br /><br /><i>14.The Litigation Master and The Monkey King</i><br /><br /><b>Momma Q</b>: I liked it.<br />I found it a little hard to follow with all the Chinese names. It made it difficult for me. I liked the story of a good man helping good people.<br /><br /><b>Dad Q</b>: I liked it.<br />I found it very good how they used songs to transport the story like travelling storytellers. I really liked it actually, I enjoy stories about sacrifices by good people. <br /><br /><b>Matt</b> I liked it.<br />You know, I should have expected some form of law-based story from Liu, who is also a practicing litigator. I wasn’t absolutely nuts for this one, but I have enjoyed the stories that aren’t SF/F and are instead about Chinese history. <br /><br />**As a follow-up to mom’s comments about the different names, they were all very similar sounding (pronounced by my unsophisticated tongue), but would be easily differentiated if reading. <br /><br /><i>15.The Man Who Ended History: A Documentary</i><br /><br /><b>Matt</b>: I LOVED this story.<br />This last one is also fairly long, so I didn’t read it to my parents, though I will probably get them to read it at their leisure in the future. Simply put: this is a harrowing and ingenious story. Liu has managed to marry the atrocities of Pingfang and Unit 731 with a sci-fi concept. In a show of immense skill, Liu examines the societal, legal, and historical consequences of the sci-fi discovery. What a way to end the collection, Liu is a master. This is why I read sci-fi.<br /><br /><br /><b>Overall</b><br /><br />What a wonderful, beautiful, powerful, and well-written collection of short stories. You’re not likely to find anything out there quite like Liu’s work. It is unique, well thought-out, and not just SF/F as billed. Instead, there’s a mix of history, literary fiction, sci-fi, fantasy, and intersections of all the aforementioned genres. It is a superb work that I’d recommend to any and all readers!<br /><br />As for the unique reading/reviewing format: also a success! I had a lot of fun discussing these stories with my parents, and it was a great way to connect over some complex ideas. It was a pleasure to bring a solitary activity into a social atmosphere, plus a lovely way to hang out with the parental units. Thanks Mom and Dad for being co-authors on this review!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12948736990489863235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_348746654" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/348746654" />
    <a title="Nataliya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya"><img alt="Nataliya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605995014p2/3672777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/348746654?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nataliya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nataliya" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya">Nataliya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781481424370" href="/book/show/27221110-the-paper-menagerie-and-other-stories">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Nataliya by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4222084-maggie">Maggie</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=shorts">shorts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=locus-winner">locus-winner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=hugo-nebula">hugo-nebula</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer348746654" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8194046752004166963">This short, bittersweet, and deceptively simple 15-page story (which you can read free <a href='http://a1018.g.akamai.net/f/1018/19022/1d/randomhouse1.download.akamai.com/19022/pdf/Paper_Menagerie.pdf' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a>) focuses on the <b>unexpected pain of trying to belong</b>, showing it through a boy's troubled relationship with his mother, viewed through the prism of cultural conflict, the inevitable clash between the old and the new, and the soft tinge of origami-shaped sadness. <blockquote>"<i> Dad had picked Mom out of a catalog."<br/>"What kind of woman puts herself into a catalog so that she can be bought? The high school me thought I kne</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText8194046752004166963" style="display:none">This short, bittersweet, and deceptively simple 15-page story (which you can read free <a href="http://a1018.g.akamai.net/f/1018/19022/1d/randomhouse1.download.akamai.com/19022/pdf/Paper_Menagerie.pdf" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>) focuses on the <b>unexpected pain of trying to belong</b>, showing it through a boy's troubled relationship with his mother, viewed through the prism of cultural conflict, the inevitable clash between the old and the new, and the soft tinge of origami-shaped sadness. <blockquote>"<i> Dad had picked Mom out of a catalog."<br>"What kind of woman puts herself into a catalog so that she can be bought? The high school me thought I knew so much about everything. Contempt felt good, like wine.</i>"</blockquote><b>The need to belong is intrinsic to all people.</b> But especially for children, it is the make-it-or-break-it need, the force that determines their viewpoints, attitudes, the way they experience the world. It is meant to be protective, help become a part of the greater whole, a part of a group, clan, society. <b>But when you come from a background very different from that of most of your peers, how do you reconcile the childhood need to belong to the majority and your heritage?</b> How do you appreciate both without resenting either one? It is immensely difficult, and immigrant children seem to so often go through the grotesquely amplified rebellion of preteen and teen years, rejecting their parents and what they represent with almost unexpected vigor, holding on to the beliefs of their new home and their 'native' peers and turning their back in shame and resentment at the 'different' that their parents signify. <blockquote>"<i>We are not other families.” I looked at him. Other families don’t have Moms who don’t belong.</i>"</blockquote>It hurts to be different as a child. And just as much it hurts for the parents to be rejected by their child, the one in whom they have hoped to preserve some of their 'old' culture and family and traditions. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380380835i/737858._SX540_.jpg" width="470" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(I love "My Big Fat Greek Wedding"! But unlike that movie, this story has none of the lighthearted attitude towards the 'otherness'. There is only sadness.)<br>----------------<blockquote>"<i>Mom looked at him. “If I say ‘love,’ I feel here." She pointed to her lips. <br>"If I say ‘ai,’ I feel here." She put her hand over her heart. <br>Dad shook his head. “You are in America.</i>"</blockquote>And this estrangement felt so very painful in the short space of this story as it was contrasted with the years of Jack's childhood when he was happily laughing at his mother's creations an playing with Laohu the Tiger - the times before he realized his <i>'difference'</i> and set out onto a determined course to change that. The course that brought him to the point when college became more important than his mother's death.<blockquote>"<i>If Mom spoke to me in Chinese, I refused to answer her. After a while, she tried to use more English. But her accent and broken sentences embarrassed me. I tried to correct her. Eventually, she stopped speaking altogether if I was around."<br><br>"Mom finally stopped making the animals when I was in high school. By then her English was much better, but I was already at that age when I wasn’t interested in what she had to say whatever language she used.</i>"</blockquote>I could easily relate to the teenage feelings of being ashamed of your parents. Isn't that feeling universal to all teenagers, protected by their maximalistic feelings of invulnerability and superiority? But the lengths to Jack goes to estrange his mother from him were so painful, so cruel that my heart was breaking for his mother whom he never understood, the differences from whom he cherished, to whom she became nothing more than an embarrassing awkward former mail-order Chinese bride, <b>little more than a reminder of what made him different from what he wanted to be - a 'native', keeping him from his <i>"all-American pursuit of happiness"</i>.</b><blockquote>"<i>You shouldn’t treat your mother that way," Dad said. But he couldn’t look me in the eyes as he said it. Deep in his heart, he must have realized that it was a mistake to have tried to take a Chinese peasant girl and expect her to fit in the suburbs of Connecticut.</i>"</blockquote>The quiet mystical element to this story - magical origami animals that came to life with the breath of Jack's mother - felt very organic and, of course, highly symbolic. I loved the quiet presence of magic, filling Jack's childhood like it is for many children, being his connection to his mother, and cruelly put away when it was no longer needed.<br><br>The only part I could have lived without was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the letter from his mother that Jack reads in the end. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It explained a lot about his mother, but in the end I felt that its well-intentioned heavy-handedness was unnecessary. The impact of this story is already strong enough without knowing all the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[horrific elements of Jack's mother's childhood and her reasons for becoming the despised by her son mail-order bride. For me, just the way her son treated her because of her 'difference' was already enough; it was cruel in a way only kids can be cruel, and she did not need to be justified to me by her difficult childhood. My heart was already breaking for her and her son, caught in the middle of the culture clash. I did not need the extra exposition <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br>----------------<br><b>4 stars.</b> A good story that takes only a few minutes to read - <a href="http://a1018.g.akamai.net/f/1018/19022/1d/randomhouse1.download.akamai.com/19022/pdf/Paper_Menagerie.pdf" rel="nofollow noopener">so go ahead and read it!</a> <br><blockquote>"<i>You know what the Chinese think is the saddest feeling in the world? It’s for a child to finally grow the desire to take care of his parents, only to realize that they were long gone.</i>"</blockquote></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8194046752004166963" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17489789017548777676" style="display:none">I rated each story separate in updates and I could make average rating but I'm not going to do that. Whole is more than sum of it's parts and as a whole this short story collection is an easy 5 stars and only short story collection that I give 5 stars that isn't written by Ray Bradbury. Best stories in this collection are among best I read overall and even "lesser" ones didn't left me indifferent.<br />In genre stories are rather diverse. There is good ol' hard sci-fi, alternative history and historical fiction, steampunk, magical realism and even noir thriller. What they do have in common are some reoccurring themes like clash of eastern and western culture, search for self identify, troubles fitting in, racism and racial prejudice. <br /><br />Favorite stories:<br />Paper menagerie<br />State change<br />Mono no aware<br /><br /><br />Honorable mentions:<br /><br />Simulacrum<br />The waves</span>

<div id="review_1548882638" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1548882638" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1548882638?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781481424370" href="/book/show/27221110-the-paper-menagerie-and-other-stories">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=animalia">animalia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=the-shorts">the-shorts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=asia">asia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1548882638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5860050015336472212">4.5 stars, rounding up. A young boy, the son of an American father and a Chinese immigrant mother, discovers that his mother has the magical gift of making origami animals that live. She makes him a lion, Laohu, a shark, and other paper animals that play and chase around their home. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455517139i/18111108.jpg' width='270' height='205' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>The details of his childhood, playing with his living origami menagerie, are delightful:<blockquote>Once, the water buffalo jumped into a dish of soy sauce on the table at dinner. (He wanted to wallow, like a real water buffalo</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText5860050015336472212" style="display:none">4.5 stars, rounding up. A young boy, the son of an American father and a Chinese immigrant mother, discovers that his mother has the magical gift of making origami animals that live. She makes him a lion, Laohu, a shark, and other paper animals that play and chase around their home. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455517139i/18111108.jpg" width="270" height="205" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The details of his childhood, playing with his living origami menagerie, are delightful:<blockquote>Once, the water buffalo jumped into a dish of soy sauce on the table at dinner. (He wanted to wallow, like a real water buffalo.) I picked him out quickly but the capillary action had already pulled the dark liquid high up into his legs. The sauce-softened legs would not hold him up, and he collapsed onto the table. I dried him out in the sun, but his legs became crooked after that, and he ran around with a limp. Mom eventually wrapped his legs in saran wrap so that he could wallow to his heart’s content (just not in soy sauce).</blockquote>But as the boy grows older, he experiences the prejudices that those who are different often suffer. Because of his loathing of everything that makes him other, he also grows ashamed of, and then distant from, his very Chinese mother.<br><br>This short story hit me hard. I was weeping by the time I finished it (the second time a story made me cry that day -- the other one was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25663807.The_Things_We_Keep" title="The Things We Keep by Sally Hepworth" rel="nofollow noopener">The Things We Keep</a>). So I made my 17 year old daughter read it while we were sitting around for half an hour, waiting for her violin recital to start. I felt kind of badly for making her tear up and risk ruining her makeup right before going on stage, but she loved it as well.<br><br>I can see why some readers fault this as being overly sentimental, but sometimes we need stories that hit us in the heart and make us appreciate people we've taken for granted. And this story will stick with me.<blockquote>“Speak English to him,” Dad said to Mom... “You have to. I’ve been too easy on you. Jack needs to fit in.”<br><br>Mom looked at him. “If I say ‘love,’ I feel here.” She pointed to her lips. “If I say ‘ai,’ I feel here.” She put her hand over her heart.</blockquote>Read it free online <a href="http://a1018.g.akamai.net/f/1018/19022/1d/randomhouse1.download.akamai.com/19022/pdf/Paper_Menagerie.pdf" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5860050015336472212" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
