<div id="review_1341357202" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1341357202" />
    <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc"><img alt="Mogsy (MMOGC)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286325553p2/4379514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1341357202?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mogsy (MMOGC)" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc">Mogsy (MMOGC)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25089595-the-paper-menagerie-and-other-stories">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=anthologies">anthologies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1341357202" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8914538376006669332">4 of 5 stars at The BiblioSanctum <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://bibliosanctum.com/2016/04/07/book-review-the-paper-menagerie-and-other-stories-by-ken-liu/'>http://bibliosanctum.com/2016/04/07/b...</a><br/><br/>One of my favorite books last year was The Grace of Kings by Ken Liu, but before he published his debut novel he was already an accomplished writer of many award-winning short stories. While in general I am not a big reader of short fiction, I’d happily make the exception for some authors’ anthologies and you can definitely bet Liu’s The Paper Menagerie and Other Stories is one of them.<br/><br/>Like many collections, there are stor</span>
  <span id="freeText8914538376006669332" style="display:none">4 of 5 stars at The BiblioSanctum <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bibliosanctum.com/2016/04/07/book-review-the-paper-menagerie-and-other-stories-by-ken-liu/">http://bibliosanctum.com/2016/04/07/b...</a><br /><br />One of my favorite books last year was The Grace of Kings by Ken Liu, but before he published his debut novel he was already an accomplished writer of many award-winning short stories. While in general I am not a big reader of short fiction, I’d happily make the exception for some authors’ anthologies and you can definitely bet Liu’s The Paper Menagerie and Other Stories is one of them.<br /><br />Like many collections, there are stories in here that I liked more than others, but overall I feel confident saying this is one of the best anthologies I have ever read. The book contains fifteen tales, showcasing a stunningly wide spread of themes and subjects. Readers of speculative fiction will enjoy stories featuring everything from artificial intelligence and virtual reality to space exploration and time travel. Many of the stories also combine these elements with influences from with cultural and historical sources, with a strong focus on Asian philosophy, mythology, and identity. Together, they come to create this profoundly heartfelt collection filled with beauty and emotion. For a more in-depth look at my thoughts on each story, please see below.<br /><br />“The Bookmaking Habits of Select Species” is the first story, kicking off the anthology with a series of imaginative and somewhat quirky reference-style descriptions of several alien approaches to reading, writing, and communication. It is a quick, experimental “tale” that teases Liu’s unique brand of creativity and promises more to come in the rest of this collection, while also providing a lighthearted opener for readers before delving into the more emotional and sorrowful stories.<br /><br />“State Change” is a story about a young woman named Rina who lives in a world where everyone’s soul manifests in a physical object from the moment you are born, from Cicero’s stone to T.S. Eliot’s coffee can. Rina’s soul is an ice cube, required to be kept close to her and frozen everywhere she goes, which understandably puts a damper on her social life. Liu uses this concept as a clever allegory to speculate how one might live with such a limitation, treating Rina’s personal journey with empathy but also some light humor.<br /><br />“The Perfect Match” was one of the better stories in this collection, imagining what a world would look like if, say, Apple and Amazon and Google all got together and decided to take over all our lives. The scary thing is that if this ever happened, we’d probably not even realize it. The story’s main character Sai shares every detail of his life with his phone so that the AI named Tilly can plan his day using his personal data to cater to his every needs, making suggestions that range from what he should have for dinner (she has a coupon!) to whom he should date. But what is a life without predictability and its surprises? As Sai grows closer to his paranoid and conspiracy theorist neighbor Jenny, he begins to question this himself.<br /><br />“Good Hunting” is a story about a father-son demon hunting team. Liang and his father are on tail of a hulijing, a kind of mischievous fox spirit in Chinese legend said take the form of beautiful women to lure unsuspecting young men. However, Liang ends up befriending a hulijing girl named Yan and discovers that magic is seeping from the world as history ushers in the age of steam and steel. As Yan loses her shapeshifting powers and Liang runs out of demons to hunt, the two reflect upon bygone times and what their futures may hold. This story hit me especially hard because I can’t help seeing it a metaphor for my own gradual abandonment of cultural traditions. My mother still observes the ritual of burning “spirit money” for the Ghost Festival like the characters do in this story, but it’s unlikely that I will continue it; I still remember the slight hint of resignation in her eyes when I told her, which strikes the same kind of melancholic tone set by this tale about cultural change.<br /><br />“The Literomancer” was probably even harder to read emotionally, because it is a sad story that ends with a punch in the gut. Lilly Dyer is a young American girl living with her expatriate parents in Taiwan in the early 1960s during the height of communist rule in China. Having not made many friends at school, Lilly immediately grows closer to a local boy named Teddy and his grandfather Mr. Kan who is literomancer, someone who reads fortunes based on written words. Mr. Kan tells Lilly stories, which she innocently repeats to her parents not understanding the unfortunate consequences that could lead to.<br /><br />“Simulacrum” explores the effects of virtual technology in this tale about Paul Larimore, the inventor of a machine capable of capturing a person’s essence and projecting it into 3D, and his relationship with his daughter, Anna Larimore. Anna is estranged from her father, and this story explains why. Interesting concept, but the ending was a little too abrupt.<br /><br />“The Regular” was my favorite story in this book, an easy 5 stars if I am rating it on its own. A perfect blend of sci-fi tech and crime noir, this is a compact tale starring Ruth, a private investigator on the trail of “The Watcher”, a serial killer who targets prostitutes—except what he’s after is not sex but something far stranger. It’s your standard murder mystery, but with its cybernetic sci-fi twist and fantastic protagonist, this one had me riveted from beginning to end, which isn’t something all mystery/thriller writers can achieve, even with full length novels.<br /><br />“The Paper Menagerie” is the titular story, and for good reason; it was the one that won Ken Liu the Hugo, Nebula and World Fantasy awards. Jack is the son of an American father and a Chinese mother who immigrated to be with her husband after he purchased her from a bride catalogue. Growing up, Jack’s mom folded elaborate origami animals that would come to life around him, but eventually he grew ashamed of these paper toys and of his Chinese heritage, preferring to play American action figures, eat American food, and speak American English in order to fit in. Again, I find it difficult sometimes to view stories like this because many of its themes hit too close to home. Suffice to say, it’s a very emotional story about cultural identity, acceptance, and growing up. Embrace those close to you and tell them how you feel; you never know when it’ll be too late.<br /><br />“An Advance Readers’ Picture Book of Comparative Cognition” follows in much the same vein as “The Bookmaking Habits of Select Species”, this time describing the different approaches to thought and communication. However, even though it contains a narrative about a woman and her child, this story didn’t quite speak to me the same way the first one did, probably because most of the descriptions of physics and technology went over my head.<br /><br />“The Waves” features Captain Maggie Chao of the generation ship Sea Foam leading her passengers on a long journey to colonize a new planet many lightyears away. To pass the time, Maggie tells stories of creation to her children. When a new discovery comes to light, the crew will have to make a decision that might affect the course of their mission and alter the future of their people. Sad to say, this is another story that didn’t make much of an impression, and was probably one of the least memorable for me in this collection.<br /><br />“Mono No Aware” is another generation ship story, featuring a group of survivors aboard the Hopeful after a massive asteroid makes impact with earth. It’s also powerful story about sacrifice and survival, but probably not as hard-hitting for me as some of the other offerings in this anthology.<br /><br />“All the Flavors (A Tale of Guan Yu, the Chinese God of War, in America)” is a cool little historical tale (though it is probably one of the longer stories in this collection) about Lily Seaver, a girl living on the frontier settlements of Idaho during the gold rush of the 1860s. Her town is happy to welcome a group of Chinese miners after a great fire wipes out most of its business and homes, for their money if not for their actual presence. Lily befriends Lao Guan, who tells her stories about Guan Yu, a deified military general worshipped by the Chinese. “All the Flavors” is different from the rest of the collection in that it veers away from sci-fi territory, focusing more on mythology and history so that this story reads more like a historical fantasy.<br /><br />“A Brief History of the Trans-Pacific Tunnel” is an alternate historical about a joint venture between Asia and the Americas to build a giant tunnel connecting the two regions. Charlie was a former foreman on the project, reliving gut-wrenching memories of his time in the construction site overseeing the work of Chinese prisoners. The completed tunnel is a work of technological wonder, but at what cost? This story proposes that great accomplishments often belie the amount of suffering and blood spilled in their achievement. It’s an interesting one, but not one of my favorites.<br /><br />“The Litigation Master and the Monkey King” was probably one of the more disappointing stories, given my high hopes for it. Few Chinese children grow up without hearing about the legend of Sun Wukong the Monkey King, and when I saw the title I don’t know what I expected, but it wasn’t this. Tian is a litigator who communes with the Monkey King. He’s also a clever and soft soul who likes to represent people from the poorer villages, and one day a woman comes to him begging for help. Instead of a cheerful take on the popular myth, this one actually takes a turn for the brutally depressing. I liked its noble themes, but it was still pretty gloomy, as it is with most of the stories in this collection.<br /><br />“The Man Who Ended History: A Documentary” closes out this anthology with a devastating look back at the atrocities committed in World War II by Unit 731, a Japanese facility that tortured and conducted human experiments on Chinese prisoners. Following the end of the war, the scientists received immunity in exchange for handling over their research. Evan Wei is a historian who is determined to use a new technology to expose these crimes against humanity to the world, calling for history to condemn the actions of Unit 731 and recognize its victims. However, this new technology has a major flaw, namely that only one person can return to the past to view a certain event, but he or she will then prevent anyone else from doing so. For a short story, this one actually contains a lot of very complex themes and philosophical dilemmas. First of foremost, the description of the kind of “time traveling” technology described here poses the question: To whom, if anyone, does history belong? A thoughtful but rather dispiriting story told in the form of a documentary transcript, “The Man Who Ended History” is a powerful conclusion that reiterates and brings together many of the themes presented in the previous fourteen tales in this collection.<br /><br />In sum, The Paper Menagerie and Other Stories is an amazing anthology, even if it is somewhat front-loaded with the more memorable stories at the beginning. Some stories worked better for me than others, that is true—but most of the tales in here are captivating in very profound ways and at times carried a personal meaning for this reviewer. I don’t often recommend short story collections, but I will for this one, and with much enthusiasm. Ken Liu’s The Paper Menagerie and Other Stories is a beautiful work of art, guaranteed to touch hearts and engage minds.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8914538376006669332" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1686201775" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5816511692942273905">I wanted to love this short story collection, but most of Ken Liu's characters fell flat. These stories contain so much good stuff: fascinating elements of science-fiction and fantasy, themes that include culture and racism and fighting for justice, surprising turns of plot that keep you on your toes - but very few of them create a lasting emotional impact. Throughout reading these individual stories, I envisioned Liu thinking "oh, this could be a really cool *insert magical realism device or un</span>
  <span id="freeText5816511692942273905" style="display:none">I wanted to love this short story collection, but most of Ken Liu's characters fell flat. These stories contain so much good stuff: fascinating elements of science-fiction and fantasy, themes that include culture and racism and fighting for justice, surprising turns of plot that keep you on your toes - but very few of them create a lasting emotional impact. Throughout reading these individual stories, I envisioned Liu thinking "oh, this could be a really cool *insert magical realism device or under-reported aspect of history* to write about" and then conjuring characters to fit his brilliant idea, rather than letting his characters drive the stories in a more organic way. Thus, while <i>The Paper Menagerie and Other Stories</i> stimulated my intellect, it failed to stir any deep feelings within my heart.<br /><br />Overall, recommended to those who want a short story collection that features many novel concepts, in particular pertaining to technology, culture, and the past and future of the human race. The collection contained a few heart-rending moments - the cultural disconnect between a mother and her son in "The Paper Menagerie," a woman who learns to melt away her inhibitions in "State Change," a daughter who refuses to forgive her father's mistakes in "Simulacrum" - but these come far and in between. Again, these stories spoke more to my brain than my heart, so if you want that type of experience, come dive right into this unique collection.</span>

  <span id="freeText4860357460073799503" style="display:none">This sounds to me like something a college sophomore would write because he's like "If I write about my heritage and sad dead mom my creative writing professor pretty much has to give me an A, right?" <tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review515892037">

<div id="review_3404014580" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3404014580" />
    <a title="Ellie (faerieontheshelf)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf"><img alt="Ellie (faerieontheshelf)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580581001p2/64075211.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3404014580?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ellie (faerieontheshelf)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ellie (faerieontheshelf)" href="/user/show/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf">Ellie (faerieontheshelf)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf?shelf=historical-set-in-the-past">historical-set-in-the-past</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf?shelf=morally-grey">morally-grey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf?shelf=short-stories-and-novellas">short-stories-and-novellas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf?shelf=much-love-so-much-love">much-love-so-much-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf?shelf=bipoc-ownvoices-fantasy">bipoc-ownvoices-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf?shelf=anthologies-and-collections">anthologies-and-collections</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf?shelf=philosophy-or-thought-provoking">philosophy-or-thought-provoking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3404014580" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3107310863882039007">Frankly, this collection of short stories is one of the best I've ever read, if not the best. It's common, when reading a short short collection, to find some stories less engaging than others, but I was invested in every story in this collection. These stories run through a gamut of genres: science fiction to fantasy to history, often combining aspects from many, but they always had a stark focus on humanity. From what makes us human to human monstrosity to culture and colonialism and how it fe</span>
  <span id="freeText3107310863882039007" style="display:none">Frankly, this collection of short stories is one of the best I've ever read, if not the best. It's common, when reading a short short collection, to find some stories less engaging than others, but I was invested in every story in this collection. These stories run through a gamut of genres: science fiction to fantasy to history, often combining aspects from many, but they always had a stark focus on humanity. From what makes us human to human monstrosity to culture and colonialism and how it feels being caught between Asian and American cultures, Ken Liu does a magnificent job in conveying this complexity. <br /><br />*<br /><br /><b> &gt; The Bookmarking Habits of Select Species </b> <i> (3.5 stars)</i><br />Something fans of Becky Chambers may enjoy, this is a short sci-fi story about different alien races and how they retain memory in their own unique ways. (Also a Nebula and Theordore Sturgeon Award finalist.)<br /><br /><b> &gt; State Change </b> <i>(4 stars)</i><br />In a world where people's souls manifest as objects, a girl lives life cautiously as her own soul is an ice cube - which when melted, may kill her. Or not. <br /><br /><b> &gt; The Perfect Match </b> <i>(5 stars)</i><br />Like an excellent episode of Black Mirror, this one is a creepy yet clever story about artificial intelligence and surveillance.<br /><br /><b> &gt; Good Hunting </b> <i>(5 stars)</i><br />This exquisitely wrought short story combines tradition with modernity as China becomes industrialised. The narrator, raised to be a demon hunter, moves to Hong Kong to become an engineer, whilst a hulijng (a nine-tailed fox) has to adapt as her magic fades, destroyed as the land is overtaken by industrial development. Particularly memorable line: "In this new age of steam and electricity, in this great metropolis [...] is anyone still in their true form."<br /><br /><b> &gt; The Literomancer </b> <i>(5 stars)</i><br />Wow, the stories in this collection just get better and better. In 1961, Lilly moves with her family from Texas to Taiwan. She befriends the kind Mr. Kan and his adopted grandson Teddy, but Lilly unintentionally lets slip information to her father over dinner that leads to both being incriminated. There's a lot of historical context behind this story - in simplest terms, to do with the Sino-American alliance and joint American-ROC covert operations against the PRC during the Cold War. The story itself is heartbreaking.<br /><br /><b> &gt; Simalcrum </b> <i>(4 stars)</i><br />A man designs the technology to make digital simulacrums/copies of people, but his use of them causes a rift between the designer and his daughter. He creates a simulacrum of her, from memories of back when she loved him, but she sees his replica of her as a violation. <br /><br /><b> &gt; The Regular </b> <i>(4 stars)</i><br />In a contemporary world similar to our own, just where cybernetic are slightly more advanced, a private investigator looks into the deaths of escorts, and the motives of the man who is killing them.<br /><br /><b> &gt; The Paper Menagerie</b> <i>(5 stars)</i><br />The titular story of the collection, 'The Paper Menagerie' is one of the shortest stories in the collection. A mother makes enchanted origami for her son, hoping for it to bring them together. But her son begins to reject his Chinese heritage when he is bullied about it, and by extension, neglects his mother. It has many different themes - the difficulty of being a Chinese-American child in America for one, but I especially liked hearing the mother's story, and her wish to remain close to her culture whilst so far for the land she grew up in. (Fun fact: this is the only story to win the Hugo, Nebula and World Fantasy awards)<br /><br /><b> &gt; An Advanced Readers' Picture Book of Comparative Cognition</b> <i> (4 stars)</i><br />It's been years since I last had to google a word to figure out what it meant, and in the first paragraph I found myself doing this twice. In this short story, a couple is pulled apart by dreams and the differing concepts of an ideal life, but for their daughter, the fact remains: <i>There are many ways to say I love you in this cold, dark universe, as many as the twinkling stars.</i><br /><br /><b> &gt; The Waves </b> <i> (4 stars)</i><br />A group sets out to colonise a future world as Earth lies dying. But when they arrive, they learn they have been surpassed by colonists who left later but arrived earlier due to technological advancement, and humanity no longer looks the same. It is a story that engages with the concept of how humanity might advance in the future, but how the concept of 'being human' may be lost along the way. (A Nebula Award finalist.)<br /><br /><b> &gt; Mono no Aware</b> <i>(4 stars)</i><br />On a dying planet, a young boy gets one of the final seats on the only ship leaving Earth. Later, he works as part of the team regulating the ship's sails, and makes a sacrifice. (Hugo Award winner)<br /><br /><b> &gt; All the Flavours</b> <i>(3.8 stars)</i><br />Based on the history of the Chinese communities that settled in Idaho during the gold rush. This one was really long, but I did like the entwined narrative strands, and the look at little-seen Chinese-American history. (Nebula Award finalist)<br /><br /><b> &gt; A Brief History of the Trans-Pacific Tunnel</b> <i>(4 stars)</i><br />Alternate history where a tunnel was built under the earth's crust during the early 1900s, linking Japan to America. Although it is alt-history, it nevertheless shines a light on the mistreatment of manual labourers that is rife throughout history.<br /><br /><b> &gt; The Litigation Master and the Monkey King</b> (<i>4 stars</i>)<br />Focusing on a crafty <i>songshi</i> who helped people out with the law during the Qing dynasty, this short story also engages with the lore of the Monkey King. But when he runs into a man who begs for his help in hiding a book filled with details about the truth of the Yangzhou Massacre, he uses his wit to ensure the truth will be known throughout history. (Nebula Award finalist)<br /><br /><b> &gt; The Man Who Ended History: A Documentary</b> <i>(5 stars)</i><br />When the ability to travel into the past is discovered, the method is used to send people back into the past, to the time when Unit 731 was operational during the Second Sino-Japanese War/WW2. It is hoped that it will help verify and confirm the presence of Unit 731, a team of Japanese doctors who partook in human experiments and mass human rights violations whilst researching biological weapons. (Finalist for the Hugo, Nebula and Theodore Sturgeon Awards.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="3107310863882039007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Claudia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20498957-claudia"><img alt="Claudia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507465969p2/20498957.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1575409836?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claudia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claudia" href="/user/show/20498957-claudia">Claudia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25089595-the-paper-menagerie-and-other-stories">review of another edition</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20498957-claudia?shelf=myths-related">myths-related</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20498957-claudia?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20498957-claudia?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20498957-claudia?shelf=asia-minus-japan">asia-minus-japan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20498957-claudia?shelf=disguised-as-sff">disguised-as-sff</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1575409836" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7776296618075745942">Initially I thought to write a few words about each story, as usual, but I realized that they would be repetitive, filled with words like awesome, great, exquisite and the like. Therefore, I'll just say that the whole collection is fascinating, mesmerizing, and superbly written. <br/><br/>He was already on a pedestal in my preferences because of his excellent translations, but after this collection I have to say his writing is flawless; he has a way with words that touches the reader deeply. Even if some </span>
  <span id="freeText7776296618075745942" style="display:none">Initially I thought to write a few words about each story, as usual, but I realized that they would be repetitive, filled with words like awesome, great, exquisite and the like. Therefore, I'll just say that the whole collection is fascinating, mesmerizing, and superbly written. <br /><br />He was already on a pedestal in my preferences because of his excellent translations, but after this collection I have to say his writing is flawless; he has a way with words that touches the reader deeply. Even if some of his stories are too sad for my taste, I cannot but acknowledge his writing skills.<br /><br />Few writers can mingle sci-fi, fantasy, magical realism, myths, history and ancient legends the way he does. I was enthralled from the first page to the last. You don't have to be a sci-fi or a fantasy fan to like this book; there is a story for everyone in it, because they are not based on technology or science, but on human condition, virtues, actions and emotions. <br /><br />With on exception (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13501217.The_Man_Who_Ended_History_A_Documentary" title="The Man Who Ended History A Documentary by Ken Liu" rel="nofollow noopener">The Man Who Ended History: A Documentary</a>), all stories here were new to me. Here is the list:<br /><br /><i>The Bookmaking Habits of Select Species<br />State Change<br />The Perfect Match<br />Good Hunting<br />The Literomancer<br />Simulacrum<br />The Regular<br />The Paper Menagerie<br />An Advanced Readers' Picture Book of Comparative Cognition<br />The Waves<br />Mono No Aware<br />All the Flavors<br />A Brief History of the Trans-Pacific Tunnel<br />The Litigation Master and the Monkey King<br />The Man Who Ended History: A Documentary</i><br /><br />I truly hope you'll give it a try; you won't be disappointed.</span>

<div id="review_3175725730" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3175725730" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3175725730?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2020-shelf">2020-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3175725730" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1520275960235219748">I'm filled with shame for not having read these fantastic short stories earlier. Instead, I just focused on reading Ken Liu's translations of Cixin Liu, and Ken Liu's own enormous epic fantasy, ignoring, (wrongly-so) his award-winning short fiction.<br/><br/>*rubs hands together and gets to work*<br/><br/>I was delighted by almost all the short, sometimes strange, fiction that filled the first pages. <br/><br/>The Bookmaking Species of Select Species tickled all my librophile instincts. <br/><br/>State Change made me change tracks HAR</span>
  <span id="freeText1520275960235219748" style="display:none">I'm filled with shame for not having read these fantastic short stories earlier. Instead, I just focused on reading Ken Liu's translations of Cixin Liu, and Ken Liu's own enormous epic fantasy, ignoring, (wrongly-so) his award-winning short fiction.<br /><br />*rubs hands together and gets to work*<br /><br />I was delighted by almost all the short, sometimes strange, fiction that filled the first pages. <br /><br />The Bookmaking Species of Select Species tickled all my librophile instincts. <br /><br />State Change made me change tracks HARD and I felt the claustrophobia and intense BELIEF behind the somewhat magical conceit that each of us has our souls trapped in a small, unique object that we must protect at all costs. The twist is in the title.<br /><br />Perfect Match made me think I had just watched a Black Mirror episode or a pretty common technothriller idea, but it wasn't bad for all that.<br /><br />Good Hunting was a freaking delight because I recognized it right away as one of my favorite on-screen adaptations in the Netflix show Love, Death, and Robots. Kitsune legend meets steampunk transformation!<br /><br />The Literomancer was both darkly interesting and pretty disturbing. Cultural Revolution meets interpretive magic.<br /><br />Simulacrum was okay. I didn't dislike it but it wasn't as poignant as some I've read on the same thing.<br /><br />The Regular was a much longer tale that was a police procedural, a mystery with a ton of great cyborg elements interwoven in the solving and the causes of the crimes. It was both clever and fast-paced and pure popcorn goodness.<br /><br />The Paper Menagerie was rather sweet and all about learning about your family and dealing with cross-cultural divides. I can appreciate it and do, but it is not my favorite story in the bunch despite all the awards it was given.<br /><br />An Advanced Readers’ Picture Book of Comparative Cognition made me oooh and ahhh because I LOVE a good story that doesn't hold back on the science and speculation and rolls all over the carpet with a cool tale.<br /><br />The Waves was pretty ok. Not the best, but definitely above average.<br /><br />Mono No Aware felt like a more traditional SF story with space travel. Also okay.<br /><br />All the Flavors rather surprised me. I didn't realize I would be getting a rather long Western set during the time of the railroad building where many Chinese lost their lives in America in the Company Towns while building the Transcontinental. It was rather great.<br /><br />A Brief History of The Trans-Pacific Tunnel was written as snippets of news articles about (somewhat) digging a hole to China. I dug this short one.<br /><br />The Litigation Master and The Monkey King might be my favorite story here. More than anything, it's a legal drama set in classic China that turns a trickster into a hero... on the side of safeguarding history. Great stuff.<br /><br />The Man Who Ended History: A Documentary felt like a very different take on the same theme, but this time it had a very cool time-travel trick that caused a LOT of trouble for the creator. What kind of trouble? The usual kind: Political, social, Denialists, national embarrassment. What is it about? Getting proof, some small apology for Japan's role in the atrocities they committed during their occupations of China and other countries during WWII. Many horrible experiments were performed on prisoners. This story is rooted in facts, but the SF portion of the tale just pulls out a new, very believable wrinkle in the ongoing nastiness. Should tragedies that are old be swept under the rug, never acknowledged, or acknowledged and in the same breath denied?<br /><br />This last one was pretty hard to get through, emotionally. Accordingly, I give it very high marks.<br /><br /><br />Overall, I loved the entire collection. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="1520275960235219748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1750510351" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1750510351" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1750510351?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19126246-kaitlin?shelf=my-sff-faves">my-sff-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19126246-kaitlin?shelf=short-story-collections">short-story-collections</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1750510351" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2208418002884046738">This is a wonderful collection of short SFF/Speculative fiction stories all written by the highly intelligent and eloquent Ken Liu. This wasn't my first time reading from Liu as I read his translation of the Three Body Problem, but this was my first time reading his own work and I was thoroughly impressed!<br/><br/>What I think I loved most about the stories within this collection is that each one felt unique and genuine. Every voice of the narrator was different and they all had differing themes and topi</span>
  <span id="freeText2208418002884046738" style="display:none">This is a wonderful collection of short SFF/Speculative fiction stories all written by the highly intelligent and eloquent Ken Liu. This wasn't my first time reading from Liu as I read his translation of the Three Body Problem, but this was my first time reading his own work and I was thoroughly impressed!<br /><br />What I think I loved most about the stories within this collection is that each one felt unique and genuine. Every voice of the narrator was different and they all had differing themes and topics that they dealt with. The SFF elements were toned down and paired back which meant that the stories felt as though they had more room to explore. I felt as though every tale had a deeper layer and meaning beneath when you looked into it.<br /><br />My favourite of the stories was The Paper Menagerie (the title story) and this is the one which won 3 amazing awards, World Fantasy, Hugo and Nebula. I loved the creativity of the tale, with origami creatures coming to life and fascinating a young child, but I also adored the heart and soul of the relationships within the story. The moments where we're left to question the child's motives and the mother's wishes, and I could feel the raw love.<br /><br />The other story which really moved me (although to be honest SO MANY of them did!) was the final one, The Man Who Ended History: A Documentary, becuase this was about Unit 731 in Pingfang, Japan. Unit 731 was an experimental facility where drugs and nasty horrible tests took place on human specimens...live ones. This is a horrendous piece of history that I had never heard of. I was astonished that not only had I not heard of it but it was hushed up for a very long time by the leaders in Japan, and sadly now that it's come to light the stories we do hear are horrific. This story touched me, it was harsh, horrific and filled with death and disinterest. I couldn't believe the reaction of some people to the claims and when I learned more about it (from my own research after finishing) I was more horrified and disgusted. I am very glad that I learned of this, people who suffered should never be forgotten...<br /><br />That's not to say that all the stories within this focus on negatives, we have space exploration, time machines, fantastical creatures and much more. I loved the way that Ken Liu clearly took influences and reference from modern day, current science. We see one story about a man who was recruited to build the Trans-Pacific Tunnel (a concept proposed in 2014 but not yet actually sanctioned) and some very cool molecular discussions. I find that science can often go over my head when we get into nitty-gritty details, but I think Liu's way of describing things is both detailed and interesting with a sense of ease too.<br /><br />On the whole there wasn't a bad story within this for me and whilst I had a few which I 'only' liked there were so many I loved I couldn't deny this a 5* rating. I would hugely recommend this to you if you want something surprising, imaginative and filled with science and fantasy. It was a unique read with the Chinese references and influences too, and all of that combined made it work so well. If Liu publishes another short story collection I will for sure be buying that one too :) Highly recommended :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2208418002884046738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1776507343" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1776507343" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7022024-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470679918p2/7022024.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1776507343?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/7022024-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25089595-the-paper-menagerie-and-other-stories">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=short-story">short-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=anthologies">anthologies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1776507343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3043920489956768954">In retrospect I decided to up this book to a full five stars. It truly was a wonderful read and had some many diverse and interesting stories within it. While perhaps not as strongly linked thematically as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1773791161' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stories of Your Life and Others</a> (also by a Chinese-American writer), they nearly all delivered on fascinating and engaging stories.<br/><br/>One common motif he employed was writing about various alien (and I mean ALIEN) species and civilizations. One story looked at how they created books (or their cul</span>
  <span id="freeText3043920489956768954" style="display:none">In retrospect I decided to up this book to a full five stars. It truly was a wonderful read and had some many diverse and interesting stories within it. While perhaps not as strongly linked thematically as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1773791161" rel="nofollow noopener">Stories of Your Life and Others</a> (also by a Chinese-American writer), they nearly all delivered on fascinating and engaging stories.<br /><br />One common motif he employed was writing about various alien (and I mean ALIEN) species and civilizations. One story looked at how they created books (or their cultural/technological equivalent), another about decisions various species would make to ensure the survival of the next generation. All had really interesting ideas for alien biology and culture.<br /><br />The other stories ram the gamut from techno thrillers that examined the pervasiveness and control of user-tailored choice algorithms to the Chinese immigrant experience in 19th century Idaho to an alternative history dealing with a transpacific tunnel with plenty more in between All had a bit of Chinese culture or perspective in them and they all offered up some interesting questions or perspectives to ponder.<br /><br />I think my two favorite were <b>Good Hunting</b>, about a very unique serial killer and the detective that tries to hunt him down and <b>The Man Who Ended History</b> which put forth a fascinating technology which allows people to experience the past directly, though at the cost of consuming that moment forever. These two stories showcased Liu's ability to write compelling characters and tense scenes as well as ability to offer up innovative ideas and extrapolate out how these ideas would change the way people acted and behaved.<br /><br />All in all a really top notch collection of short stories that will keep you fascinated and engaged throughout. Check out my status updates for a mini-run down of each story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3043920489956768954" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2176682718" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2176682718" />
    <a title="TS Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan"><img alt="TS Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543800303p2/30279227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2176682718?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781784975692" href="/book/show/32295221-the-paper-menagerie-and-other-stories">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=physical-owned">physical-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2176682718" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10250556697137343155"><b>4.5 stars.</b><br/><br/>I've been meaning to read Ken Liu's collection of short stories for a quite a while. His translation for two of Cixin Liu's books in the Remembrance of Earth's Past trilogy was excellent and I've heard a lot of great things about the titular short story of this collection.<br/><br/>In my opinion, the preface alone warrants at least a 5-star and an award. Liu's writing is utterly beautiful and profound, and one can clearly see how talented and intelligent this author is just from reading his pref</span>
  <span id="freeText10250556697137343155" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars.</b><br /><br />I've been meaning to read Ken Liu's collection of short stories for a quite a while. His translation for two of Cixin Liu's books in the Remembrance of Earth's Past trilogy was excellent and I've heard a lot of great things about the titular short story of this collection.<br /><br />In my opinion, the preface alone warrants at least a 5-star and an award. Liu's writing is utterly beautiful and profound, and one can clearly see how talented and intelligent this author is just from reading his preface to the collection. I've highlighted at least half of it because it was so well-written.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>"Every act of communication is a miracle of translation.</strong>
  </em>
  <br />
  <br />
  <em>
    <strong>... And yet, whatever has been lost in translation in the long journey of my thoughts through the maze of civilization to your mind, I think you do understand me, and you think you do understand me. Our minds managed to touch, if but briefly and imperfectly.</strong>
  </em>
  <br />
  <em>
    <strong>Does the thought not make the universe seem just a bit kinder, a bit brighter, a bit warmer and more human?</strong>
  </em>
  <br />
  <em>
    <strong>We live for such miracles."</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote><br />It was my intention to read Paper Menagerie and Other Stories slowly; no more than a story a day. Below are my brief thoughts right after I finished each one.<br /><br /><u>The Bookmaking Habits of Select Species</u><br /><br /><em>5 stars</em> - such an inventive, profound and thought-provoking piece. I'm in awe with Ken Liu's mind on crafting this brilliant narrative about the various methods of creating and consuming books.  These allegories drawn from alien manifestations are still completely relatable to human beings.<br /><br /><u>State Change</u><br /><br /><em>4.5 stars</em> - what an original and emotional story about souls being represented by inanimate objects. Objects that truly represent the aura of the person whose soul it contains.<br /><br /><u>The Perfect Match</u><br /><br /><em>4 stars</em> - a relevant story about how internet giants are taking over our lives. Amazon, Facebook, Google are pretty much synonymous with vast data sharing, 24/7 surveillance and consumer targeting algorithms. I think if I've not read quite a few other great short stories with a similar theme, this would have had even more of an impact.<br /><br /><u>Good Hunting</u><br /><br /><em>4 stars</em> - an imaginative and though-provoking narrative on the transformation of the world from old magic (supernatural) to new magic (technology).<br /><br /><u>Literomancer</u><br /><br /><em>4.5 stars</em> - wow, this was beautiful and brutally sad in equal measure. A really well-written short story about literomancy, racism and the revolution against Communism in Taiwan.<br /><br /><u>Simulacrum</u><br /><br /><em>4 stars</em> - this story about a camera being able to capture a person into a simulation of a particular moment was deeply affecting. It is both disturbing and very poignant. Told from two perspectives of a father and his daughter.<br /><br /><u>The Regular</u><br /><br /><em>3.5 stars</em> - a decent murder mystery with emotion suppression as its core theme. Is it ever a good idea to suppress emotions, be it fear, grief or rage?<br /><br /><u>Paper Menagerie</u><br /><br /><em>5 stars</em> - magical, emotional and poignant, Ken Liu managed to hit really hard in just 15 pages. This short story deserved all its awards, and it's a must-read.<br /><br /><em>Note: If you want to read this extraordinary short story to get a taste of Liu's genius, you can do so <a href="https://io9.gizmodo.com/read-ken-lius-amazing-story-that-swept-the-hugo-nebula-5958919" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</em><br /><br /><u>Advanced Readers' Picture Book of Comparative Cognition</u><br /><br /><em>4 stars</em> - another profound piece of writing where Ken Liu created comparative cognition between various alien species and humans; concept of memory, falling in love, depletion of natural resources, and parental control/decision. One of the more hard sci-fi entries in the collection.<br /><br /><u>The Waves</u><br /><br /><em>5 stars</em> - wow, yet another profound piece that juxtaposed creation myths against a story of humans becoming immortal as they sought the stars and explore the universe. It became so surreal until the last moment when the story came full circle back to creation.<br /><br /><u>Mono No Aware</u><br /><br /><em>4.5 stars</em> - a beautiful story about the transcience of life in the universe told with Japanese sensibilities.<br /><br /><u>All the Flavors</u><br /><br /><em>4 stars</em> - the longest story in the collection, it depicted the settlement of the Chinese in the America as they sought make their fortune in a country known to them as Old Gold Mountain. Woven through the frame story was a tale of Guan Yu, a deified military general worshipped as the God of War by the Chinese.<br /><br /><u>A Brief History of the Trans-Pacific Tunnel</u><br /><br /><em>4 stars</em> - an alternate history piece where Japan proposed to connect the major Eastern cities to America with a tunnel under the Pacific ocean. While a marvellous achievement, the Trans-Pacific Tunnel was constructed at a huge cost, in every sense of the word. A pointed allegory of humanity's capacity to do whatever it takes for advancement.<br /><br /><u>The Litigation Master and The Monkey King</u><br /><br /><em>4 stars</em> - a bleak and depressing story that commemorated those who suffered under the brutality of the Manchu rulers in China. The addition of The Monkey King added a most unusual conflicting tone of irreverence to the bleak narrative.<br /><br /><u>The Man Who Killed History: A Documentary</u><br /><br /><em>5 stars</em> - a very powerful and thought-provoking narrative that evoked the horrors and atrocities committed in Pingfang by Unit 731 during the Second Sino-Japanese War. A brilliant science fiction piece where the concept of quantum entanglement enabled time travel back in time to revisit history; history that had been sanitised or altogether silenced for political gain and power. Another must-read alongside with the titular story.<br /><br />As with most collections, the quality inevitably varies from one story to another. Regardless, as a collective, they echo the same theme, and that is the importance of stories, regardless of which genre it came in. The majority of these short pieces were incredibly moving. That Ken Liu managed to convey so much through so few words is a testament of his immense talent and the profundity of his imagination.  His writing is evocative with an Eastern-like grace which is understated yet heartbreaking. The Paper Menagerie and Other Stories is an enchanting collection of short stories that is meant to be savoured time and again.<br /><br /><br /><b>You can purchase the book from: <u><a href="https://www.amazon.co.uk/Paper-Menagerie-Ken-Liu-ebook/dp/B015Q7V9C4/" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon UK</a></u> | <u><a href="https://www.amazon.com/Paper-Menagerie-Other-Stories-ebook/dp/B00TBKYK60/" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon US</a></u> | <u><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/book/9781509813025/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository (Free shipping)</a></u>| <u><a href="https://bookshop.org/books/the-paper-menagerie-and-other-stories/9781481424363" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookshop.Org</a></u></b><br /><br /><i>You can find <a href="https://wp.me/pa0WBY-1wM" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> and my other reviews at <a href="http://novelnotions.net/category/book-reviews/tss-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions.</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10250556697137343155" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_309479728" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/309479728" />
    <a title="Flannery" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/652877-flannery"><img alt="Flannery" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312843258p2/652877.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/309479728?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Flannery" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Flannery" href="/user/show/652877-flannery">Flannery</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781481424370" href="/book/show/27221110-the-paper-menagerie-and-other-stories">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Flannery by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=shorts">shorts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer309479728" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14809532472181774408">This short story won the 2011 Nebula Prize for Short Fiction. <i>The Paper Menagerie</i> is a very quick 15 or so page read about a young man's relationship with his mother. The narrator is half American/half Chinese and his mother came to live in the suburbs of Connecticut as a mail order bride. He can't understand why she was ever a mail order bride, why his father married her, and why she won't learn English or try harder to fit into American culture. The strongest connection between mother and son </span>
  <span id="freeText14809532472181774408" style="display:none">This short story won the 2011 Nebula Prize for Short Fiction. <i>The Paper Menagerie</i> is a very quick 15 or so page read about a young man's relationship with his mother. The narrator is half American/half Chinese and his mother came to live in the suburbs of Connecticut as a mail order bride. He can't understand why she was ever a mail order bride, why his father married her, and why she won't learn English or try harder to fit into American culture. The strongest connection between mother and son existed when he was younger and his mom folded an elaborate menagerie of origami animals that were infused with a touch of magic for him, which he played with all the time. As the boy grew up, though, he felt more pressure to leave his Chinese heritage behind to fit in with his peers. <br /><br />Sometimes short stories are able to elicit emotions in a quick and strong way, a real punch. This story is like that. By the end, I just felt awful...and I'm happy about it. <a href="http://a1018.g.akamai.net/f/1018/19022/1d/randomhouse1.download.akamai.com/19022/pdf/Paper_Menagerie.pdf" rel="nofollow noopener">Just go read it.</a> (or you can listen to it at the link Tatiana left in the comments)</span>
  <a data-text-id="14809532472181774408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2174881966" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2174881966" />
    <a title="Lindsay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay"><img alt="Lindsay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588746288p2/10326608.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2174881966?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay">Lindsay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2174881966" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6054907606482446012">An amazing collection of Ken Liu's shorter work that is always moving but often harrowing, and at its most disturbing when he turns his beautiful prose to historical events.<br/><br/>This collection includes the brilliant "Mono No Aware", set on a lightsail spaceship fleeing a destroyed Earth and the emotionally gutting "The Paper Menagerie", dealing with the relationship a half-Chinese man has with his Chinese mother. Both of these are Hugo winners, but they're far from the only brilliant stories in the </span>
  <span id="freeText6054907606482446012" style="display:none">An amazing collection of Ken Liu's shorter work that is always moving but often harrowing, and at its most disturbing when he turns his beautiful prose to historical events.<br /><br />This collection includes the brilliant "Mono No Aware", set on a lightsail spaceship fleeing a destroyed Earth and the emotionally gutting "The Paper Menagerie", dealing with the relationship a half-Chinese man has with his Chinese mother. Both of these are Hugo winners, but they're far from the only brilliant stories in the collection, with my other favorites being "The Waves" and the historical fiction piece "The Literomancer".</span>
  <a data-text-id="6054907606482446012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1553630218" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1553630218" />
    <a title="Jenny (Reading Envy)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy"><img alt="Jenny (Reading Envy)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455391853p2/68030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1553630218?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny (Reading Envy)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny (Reading Envy)" href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy">Jenny (Reading Envy)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=read2016">read2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=goodreads-giveaway">goodreads-giveaway</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1553630218" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9905465373980212352">I will keep track of notes of the stories as I go since I'm reading this between other things.<br/><br/><i>The Bookmaking Habits of Select Species</i><br/>More about storytelling and how our sense of being informs how we save and tell stories, I know I've read this one before. The ideas are very imaginative.<br/><br/><i>State Change</i><br/>What if your soul were a cigarette box, or an ice cube? What happens when you smoke the last one or the ice melts?<br/><br/><i>The Perfect Match</i><br/>The dangers of what we trade for our privacy. This was a bit preachy b</span>
  <span id="freeText9905465373980212352" style="display:none">I will keep track of notes of the stories as I go since I'm reading this between other things.<br /><br /><i>The Bookmaking Habits of Select Species</i><br />More about storytelling and how our sense of being informs how we save and tell stories, I know I've read this one before. The ideas are very imaginative.<br /><br /><i>State Change</i><br />What if your soul were a cigarette box, or an ice cube? What happens when you smoke the last one or the ice melts?<br /><br /><i>The Perfect Match</i><br />The dangers of what we trade for our privacy. This was a bit preachy but I still liked it! The end is nigh.<blockquote>"Surveillance is surveillance. I can never understand why some people think it matters whether it's the government doing it to you or a company."<br /><br />"You grew up believing you were free, which made it even harder for you to see when you weren't. You were like frogs in the pot being slowly boiled."</blockquote><i>Good Hunting</i><br />A hulijing (female demon-fox shape shifter) and her journey to becoming a cyborg? Okay. :)<br /><br /><i>The Literomancer</i><br />The power of words, set in Taiwan, with a young girl navigating a new language and culture. Plus the magic of literomancy. And illustrated by Chinese characters throughout (as in letters.)<br /><br /><i>Simulacrum</i><br />I suppose if our family members disappoint us, we can always just speak to a virtual version of them, preserved in time. Or, if we disappoint them. <br /><br /><i>The Regular</i><br />Cyber eyes, prostitutes, a truly noir detective story set in near-future Chinatown.<br /><br /><i>The Paper Menagerie</i> <br />A story I've read and loved before, about mothers, how we can fail them, how they create magic anyway.<br /><br /><i>An Advanced Readers' Picture Book of Comparative Cognition</i><br />I ended up skimming this one because it felt like one description of an imagined alien race after another, without a lot going on otherwise. <br /><br /><i>The Waves</i><br />This is probably my favorite first-read of the collection (some of these I had read previously.) It harkens back to Olaf Stapledon with the million-trillion-infinity years perspective of the universe, but following one character who evolves and migrates and turns into a creator herself. <br /><br /><i>Mono No Aware</i><br />A reread, from award nominees. The last Japanese person in the universe.<br /><br />Going to skip a few that I skimmed, but one is about torture and one is a western (?)<br /><br /><i>A Brief History of the Trans-Pacific Tunnel</i><br />An alternate history of the post-Depression era, where Japan and the United States united to carve a tunnel through the earth. Told from the perspective of one of the tunnelers, who has his own secrets.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9905465373980212352" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3029599161" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3029599161" />
    <a title="Gabrielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6753400-gabrielle"><img alt="Gabrielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598976963p2/6753400.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3029599161?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabrielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabrielle" href="/user/show/6753400-gabrielle">Gabrielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781481424363" href="/book/show/27206431-the-paper-menagerie-and-other-stories">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=own-a-copy">own-a-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3029599161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer562367530429975869">How often does this happen : you have barely passed the introduction of a book and you feel your heart swelling with that very particular feeling of love for the words that drives bookworms such as myself to pile up books in every nook and cranny of the house. Well, this is what happened to me when I curled up in bed one evening last week with Ken Liu’s collection “The Paper Menagerie”. On top of being a very talented author, Mr. Liu is also a translator, and as such, he has a grasp over a layer</span>
  <span id="freeText562367530429975869" style="display:none">How often does this happen : you have barely passed the introduction of a book and you feel your heart swelling with that very particular feeling of love for the words that drives bookworms such as myself to pile up books in every nook and cranny of the house. Well, this is what happened to me when I curled up in bed one evening last week with Ken Liu’s collection “The Paper Menagerie”. On top of being a very talented author, Mr. Liu is also a translator, and as such, he has a grasp over a layer of subtlety about word use that I think unilingual writers usually don’t have. The act of translating, of substituting a word in one language for a word in a different one, is a very delicate and tricky process, which means every word must be chosen with extreme care, and I knew right away that every word in the book I held in my hands had been chosen with deliberation, in full knowledge of every possible facet of its meaning.<br /><br />The themes of immigration, family, transhumanism, identity and belonging are in almost every short story or novella in this collection, and you can feel the very personal impact of these issues on the characters – and on yourself. The prose is elegant and rich with meaning and feelings, without ever falling into saccharine sentimentality, though it did make me cry on a couple of occasions. There’s a Bradbury-esque quality to this collection, perhaps because of the wistfulness, the gentle pull of a simpler past on the characters, of their longing for a home that doesn’t exist anymore. Liu has an incredible imagination: his surreal aliens, his retelling of Chinese myths and how he weaves them into history, his homage to the simple, yet magical things that create bonds between people.<br /><br />I would be hard press to pick a favorite, but it must be said that the title story is an absolute gem about the strange disconnect that can happen between parent and child and the challenges of communicating and growing up. “The Perfect Match” is as eerie as the best “Black Mirror” episodes, “The Regular” is a great spin on the classic trope of private investigator with substance abuse issues, and "The Man Who Ended History" is an inventive and devastating tale about time travel, war and cultural patrimony. The truth is that there is not a bad story in here, and that any fan of literary speculative fiction owes it to themselves to check this out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="562367530429975869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7943729575096691668">Despite a shaky start — a thoughtful story that’s a tad too clinical for my liking — this collection blew me away. Ken Liu talks in the preface about prizing the logic of metaphors and you can see how carefully he prizes that in his stories. Nearly every one works on multiple levels without feeling heavy handed. Some stories he manages to write historical fiction that’s somehow science fiction at the same time, others are straight ahead sci-fi thrillers that could easily warrant an entire book. </span>
  <span id="freeText7943729575096691668" style="display:none">Despite a shaky start — a thoughtful story that’s a tad too clinical for my liking — this collection blew me away. Ken Liu talks in the preface about prizing the logic of metaphors and you can see how carefully he prizes that in his stories. Nearly every one works on multiple levels without feeling heavy handed. Some stories he manages to write historical fiction that’s somehow science fiction at the same time, others are straight ahead sci-fi thrillers that could easily warrant an entire book. <br /><br />I tore through the collection and found myself surprised at the risks Liu was willing to take, yet still somehow managed to pull it all off. Magical realism, cultural commentary, steampunk, old-school sci-fi, historical fiction, cyber noir it’s all here and all wonderfully done. </span>
