<div id="review_2102654058" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2102654058" />
    <a title="Netta" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42124025-netta"><img alt="Netta" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501568994p2/42124025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2102654058?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Netta" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Netta" href="/user/show/42124025-netta">Netta</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42124025-netta?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2102654058" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3920223885490925720">Short stories are not my cup of tea. Usually I stumble upon the collection containing few pure gems and plenty of minor things which I find neither charming nor representative. Hence I finally drew the conclusion that I should never begin the acquaintance with a new author with short stories, setting them aside till I’m sure their creator and me are getting on. Ken Liu is an exeption in this regard and exceptional in every other. <br/><br/><i>The Paper Menagerie and Other Stories</i> is a collection of poignant </span>
  <span id="freeText3920223885490925720" style="display:none">Short stories are not my cup of tea. Usually I stumble upon the collection containing few pure gems and plenty of minor things which I find neither charming nor representative. Hence I finally drew the conclusion that I should never begin the acquaintance with a new author with short stories, setting them aside till I’m sure their creator and me are getting on. Ken Liu is an exeption in this regard and exceptional in every other. <br /><br /><i>The Paper Menagerie and Other Stories</i> is a collection of poignant stories, carefully crafted from delicate words and vivid images which need no further decoration. Ken Liu employs what he knows and what probably troubles him and creates a piece of wonderful, glorious prose where every minor problem, every topic touched upon becomes all of a sudden relatable and universal. The opening story, <i>The Bookmaking Habits of Select Species</i>, is an epitome of how we read and how we treat what we read. Surely, this is the best opening one can imagine for this collection. There are, of course, some minor stories that I failed to love (though I did my best!) but I take the blame. The reason is that I’m not really into Sci-Fi no matter how deep and meaningful it is. What I prefer to concentrate on writing this review is the gems that I discovered reading the book, the stories I would remember and cherish because they made me cry or smile or think. They made me feel myself a part of something huge and universal which does not acknowledge cultural or social differences. These stories take you to the world of Ken Liu’s imagination and give you terrifying, grandiose visions of the future that hopefully would never be or the past that would better not existed. Or it takes you to the place crowded with myths, magic and imaginary beings. These stories aren’t equally good but they are very well written nonetheless and those that find a way to your heart will be worth spending time on this book. <br /><br />I’m going to give you two examples of what you may find in this book by sharing with you two gems that I’ve found in this journey. The first one is the story which gave the title to this book. <i>The Paper Menagerie</i> is what I’d call a private tragedy. It’s the story of a Chinese mother making paper animals for her desperately longing to be an American son and powerful magic of memory and love which slowly unfolds in the middle of American dream. The second one is the devastating story of time travel, Unit 731 and a man who wanted to change the way people perceive history. <i>The Man Who Ended History: A Documentary</i> is a perfect example of how one can employ Sci-Fi tools to tell the story which keep ringing in your ears like a bell. <i>”There are no monsters. The monster is us”</i>, says Ken Liu. I’m sad to admit he’s right. <br /><br />In between these two stories you will find plenty of fantastic stuff. The story of what an old man can do with words when a bit of decent magic is involved. The story of love which became an object, mere shadow of reality. The story of the future where people are dominated by the machine. And many more stories embodying elegant, powerful prose. In the end, all of them are just one bigger than life story of injustice, and <i>“one has to be careful, whenever one tells a story about a great injustice”</i>, and one happened to be brilliant. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3920223885490925720" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1367370624" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1367370624" />
    <a title="Bob/Sally" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2224905-bob-sally"><img alt="Bob/Sally" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598307870p2/2224905.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1367370624?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bob/Sally" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bob/Sally" href="/user/show/2224905-bob-sally">Bob/Sally</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2224905-bob-sally?shelf=fantasy-historical">fantasy-historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2224905-bob-sally?shelf=alternate-history">alternate-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2224905-bob-sally?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1367370624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8510550366778250737">As much as I wanted to love The Paper Menagerie and Other Stories, I have to be honest in that I only thought it was okay. I mean, I can see how these stories established a reputation for Ken Liu, and there’s no doubt that some of them are indeed award worthy, but I didn’t connect with nearly as many as I would have liked.<br/><br/>Before you start getting disappointed, however, let me say that I blame the format, not necessarily the content. I’ve always been drawn to doorstopper fantasy novels like The G</span>
  <span id="freeText8510550366778250737" style="display:none">As much as I wanted to love The Paper Menagerie and Other Stories, I have to be honest in that I only thought it was okay. I mean, I can see how these stories established a reputation for Ken Liu, and there’s no doubt that some of them are indeed award worthy, but I didn’t connect with nearly as many as I would have liked.<br /><br />Before you start getting disappointed, however, let me say that I blame the format, not necessarily the content. I’ve always been drawn to doorstopper fantasy novels like The Grace of Kings, where we have six or seven hundred pages to immerse ourselves in the world, so it’s not a surprise that many of these stories fell flat or felt a little shallow.<br /><br />Having said all that, I’d be remiss if I didn’t heap some praise on those stories that did work for me.<br /><br /><i>“State Change”</i> hooked me from the start, with a young woman’s strange obsession with freezers, glaciers, and ice cubes. Rina lives in a world where our souls physically manifest as small items that we must keep close at all times, which is easy enough if your soul is a rock or a cigarette package, not so much when it’s something as fragile as an ice cube. It’s the subtle twists at the end, however, where there magic happens.<br /><br /><i>“Good Hunting”</i> was probably my favorite in the collection, being a story about ghosts, demons, steam-trains, and eternal change. Once a world of magic and monsters, China has seen all of that disappear as the railroad makes its way across the land. Faced with the loss of his family’s legacy, Liang befriends a young shapeshifter and comes to understand the nature of change and the mechanics of being an agent of change.<br /><br /><i>“The Regular”</i> is a story I didn’t expect much out of, as crime stories and murder mysteries really aren’t my thing, but then we learn that Regulators are . . . and what they’ve done to Ruth’s capacity for emotion. There is a lot going on in this story, with much of it either in the past or beneath the surface of the narrative, and the climax is one of the most powerful scenes in the collection.<br /><br /><i>“A Brief History of the Trans-Pacific Tunnel”</i> is comprised of stories within stories, with excerpts from A Brief History of the Trans-Pacific Tunnel (1960) and The Ignoramus’s Guide to American History (1995) interspersed within the tale of interracial romance, with one man’s reminiscing being the final, darkest piece that brings it all together.<br /><br />An uneven collection (for me, at least), that was far heavier on politics, history, and sociology than I anticipated, The Paper Menagerie and Other Stories didn’t amaze me like The Grace of Kings did, but it may be the perfect appetizer for those not yet ready to commit to one doorstopper with another on the way later this year.<br /><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Thanks to Saga Press for providing me with a copy of this book in exchange for my honest review. This does not affect my opinion of the book or the content of my review.</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="8510550366778250737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div id='comments_for_review_1367370624' style='display: none;'>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1486176134" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1486176134" />
    <a title="Andreas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20379307-andreas"><img alt="Andreas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512938270p2/20379307.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1486176134?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andreas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andreas" href="/user/show/20379307-andreas">Andreas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20379307-andreas?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1486176134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12419361404028828436"><i>Review at my <a href='http://wp.me/p4QI2m-lW' rel='nofollow noopener'>blog</a>.</i><br/><br/>Merged review:<br/><br/><i>This is only a summary of the full reviews of the stories in this collection. You'll find detailed reviews at my <a href='http://wp.me/p4QI2m-l9' rel='nofollow noopener'>blog</a>.</i><br/><br/>I've previously read Lius's story <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24972424.The_Regular' title='The Regular by Ken Liu' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Regular</a> and his last year's novel <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18952341.The_Grace_of_Kings__The_Dandelion_Dynasty___1_' title='The Grace of Kings (The Dandelion Dynasty, #1) by Ken Liu' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Grace of Kings</a>. Both make me think that this could be a must-read. I went first to the eponymous story <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13501210.The_Paper_Menagerie' title='The Paper Menagerie by Ken Liu' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Paper Menagerie</a> and after a couple of stories, I realized the author's diversity in style and topics: I became a fan of this author, as you'll never get bored, be it t</span>
  <span id="freeText12419361404028828436" style="display:none"><i>Review at my <a href="http://wp.me/p4QI2m-lW" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a>.</i><br /><br />Merged review:<br /><br /><i>This is only a summary of the full reviews of the stories in this collection. You'll find detailed reviews at my <a href="http://wp.me/p4QI2m-l9" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a>.</i><br /><br />I've previously read Lius's story <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24972424.The_Regular" title="The Regular by Ken Liu" rel="nofollow noopener">The Regular</a> and his last year's novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18952341.The_Grace_of_Kings__The_Dandelion_Dynasty___1_" title="The Grace of Kings (The Dandelion Dynasty, #1) by Ken Liu" rel="nofollow noopener">The Grace of Kings</a>. Both make me think that this could be a must-read. I went first to the eponymous story <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13501210.The_Paper_Menagerie" title="The Paper Menagerie by Ken Liu" rel="nofollow noopener">The Paper Menagerie</a> and after a couple of stories, I realized the author's diversity in style and topics: I became a fan of this author, as you'll never get bored, be it tin-foiled sharks or atrocities from Unit 731. Liu often contrasts Western and Eastern culture, placing a Chinese woman in the midst of USA in his awards winning story The Paper Menagerie, or the other way round, placing a U.S. family in the counterintelligence cold war of Taiwan's 60s in The Literomancer. But don't reduce the author to this topic alone: The stories' genres vary between magical realism (State Change), steampunk (Good Hunting), near future SF (The Regular, Simulacrum) or dystopia (The Perfect Match). I didn't find horror stories in it, although they are sometimes at the border to it, e.g. when describing torture scenes like in The Literomancer. This sometimes bleak realism contrasts fascinating magic or unreal setting which creep into the story, like in State Change where souls manifest in real objects.<br /><br />Lius's publication frequency exploded since 2010, the collection contains only one story State Change from 2004 before that year. Now that he started his novels from the Dandelion War, Liu said that he won't publish that many shorter works any more. An exception would be the excellent, but previously unpublished story An Advanced Reader’s Picture Book of Comparative Cognition which will delight old fans and new. In this sense, the collection is a kind of retrospective and I can fully recommend it.<br /><br />One constant factor remains: How many U.S. girls curious about Chinese culture will crawl out of Liu's pen?</span>
  <a data-text-id="12419361404028828436" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1301260802" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1301260802" />
    <a title="ᴥ Irena ᴥ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5252054-irena"><img alt="ᴥ Irena ᴥ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425497470p2/5252054.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1301260802?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ᴥ Irena ᴥ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ᴥ Irena ᴥ" href="/user/show/5252054-irena">ᴥ Irena ᴥ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781481424370" href="/book/show/27221110-the-paper-menagerie-and-other-stories">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5252054-irena?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1301260802" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8900351802011265573">I don't remember when I read this. I do remember the overwhelming sadness it left behind though. <br/>This is a short story about a boy whose mother is a mail order bride from Hong Kong. It is also a story of prejudices and a boy's shame. He wished her to be the same as everyone around them. <br/><br/>It would take years for the collection of origami animals made by his mother when he was a child to come alive and give him a special message. Beautiful and heartbreaking at the same time.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3119497261" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3119497261" />
    <a title="jade" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11030012-jade"><img alt="jade" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562419355p2/11030012.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3119497261?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jade" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jade" href="/user/show/11030012-jade">jade</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">sci-fi fans interested in the blend/link between different cultures</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to jade by: </span>
      a Popular Short Sci-Fi Stories list, which was 100% correct
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11030012-jade?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11030012-jade?shelf=diverse-rep">diverse-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11030012-jade?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3119497261" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6412359523249223257">short story collections are always challenging to review. <br/><br/>that said, with this blend of sci-fi, magical realism, history, and speculative fiction in general, ken liu has done something <i>amazing</i>. he explores themes of <b>individual</b> identity and <b>cultural</b> identity, the merging between the two, and looks at the humanity of expression by deconstructing language.<br/><br/>some stories are short and simple. others are infinitely more layered. all of them are heartrending in various ways. one of the main themes echoi</span>
  <span id="freeText6412359523249223257" style="display:none">short story collections are always challenging to review. <br /><br />that said, with this blend of sci-fi, magical realism, history, and speculative fiction in general, ken liu has done something <i>amazing</i>. he explores themes of <b>individual</b> identity and <b>cultural</b> identity, the merging between the two, and looks at the humanity of expression by deconstructing language.<br /><br />some stories are short and simple. others are infinitely more layered. all of them are heartrending in various ways. one of the main themes echoing throughout is the ability to <b>adapt and cope</b> with big shifts in perspective and culture, particularly between east and west.<br /><br />above all, liu shows how incredibly adaptive he is with this; his tone, his word use, everything changes to fit the atmosphere and expression of a story. in that sense, he’s like the themes he describes -- always cognizant of <b>language</b> and how to use it. i loved watching him flex writing a sweet, relatable western and then coming in hot with surrealist soul-searching, hard sci-fi, or swap to a hardboiled detective story.<br /><br />the stories closest to our own history that take inspiration from <b>real world events</b> hit the hardest. he uncovers some of the darkest bits of our world’s war crimes and its abundant racism.<br /><br />in terms of criticism, some of these stories are a bit <b>baity</b> in an emotional way without offering the necessary depth or nuance to fully appreciate them. kind of like one of those Sad commercials that sets you up for a teary-eyed moment and you cry, even though you know the product seller’s playing you.<br /><br />but regardless of that, i believe these stories <b>need to be told</b>. let’s be fair: this anthology provides powerful material for anyone regarding mixed asian cultures and heritage. so i really don’t mind that some of these tales are home to a couple of hallmark/lifetime moments.<br /><br />because really, it’s harrowing having one foot in and one foot out the door of a culture. liu’s ability to highlight several aspects of this through examining both the <b>happy merging</b> of cultures and <b>forced assimilation</b> of them is fantastic. i’ll be the first to admit that i ugly cried a couple of times during this.<br /><br />in conclusion, a great speculative fiction anthology. i can totally get why people are raving about this. <br /><br />you can find the reviews for every <b>individual</b> story down below! no spoilers, just hiding behind the tag so the review’s scroll-friendly.<br /><br />✎ <i>4.0 stars total.</i><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <br />
  <b>THE BOOKMAKING HABITS OF SELECT SPECIES</b>
  <br />
  <blockquote>✎ <i>3.0 stars.</i><br /><i><b>pockets of sentience glow in the cold, deep void of the universe like bubbles in a vast, dark sea.</b></i><br /><br />this story is about how every species in the universe finds a way to make books; how they do it, and what it means to them. cute &amp; thoughtful, and also interesting from a writer’s perspective.<br /></blockquote>
  <b>STATE CHANGE</b>
  <br />
  <blockquote>✎ <i>4.0 stars.</i><br /><b><i>all life is an experiment.</i></b><br /><br />what is a soul, truly, and how does it change? do we spend ourselves as we live, and what is the impression we choose to give? these are matters of life and death, especially if your soul is contained by an ice cube ready to melt at a moment’s notice.<br /></blockquote>
  <b>THE PERFECT MATCH</b>
  <br />
  <blockquote>✎ <i>3.0 stars.</i><br /><b><i>in the face of the inevitable, the only choice is to adapt.</i></b><br /><br />so what if a siri or an alexa was installed everywhere around the world, and one private company owned all the data? would we still be ourselves, when constantly guided by an algorithm that knows all our secret desires? kind of a common theme in speculative sci-fi, but still handled well.<br /></blockquote>
  <b>GOOD HUNTING</b>
  <br />
  <blockquote>✎ <i>4.0 stars.</i><br /><b><i>a terrible thing had been done to me, but i could also be terrible.</i></b><br /><br />culture and technology stand in seemingly direct opposites to each other in this tale; how can you cope with technological advancement, especially when forced upon you by colonizers who destroy your culture while they’re at it? you make it yours.<br /></blockquote>
  <b>THE LITEROMANCER</b>
  <br />
  <blockquote>✎ <i>3.5 stars.</i><br /><b><i>the chinese are like wildflowers, and they will survive and make joy wherever they go.</i></b><br /><br />more of a historical fiction story, this one absolutely broke my heart. it takes place in taiwan during the sixties at the height of the cold war, and follows a red-haired texan girl as she makes friends with a local chinese literomancer (someone who can divine through the shapes and parts of words) and his adopted grandson.<br /></blockquote>
  <b>SIMULACRUM</b>
  <br />
  <blockquote>✎ <i>3.5 stars.</i><br /><b><i>in your mind, you traced that captured image again and again, until the person was erased by the stencil.</i></b><br /><br />the classic “is the love we receive from projections/holograms of people real?”. only now contrasted deeply between a father who once found solace in the arms of projected women and claimed it wasn’t cheating, and a daughter who caught her father in the act and refuses to see him as anything else than what she saw in that single moment.<br /></blockquote>
  <b>THE REGULAR</b>
  <br />
  <blockquote>✎ <i>4.0 stars.</i><br /><b><i>evil has to be confronted dispassionately.</i></b><br /><br />a detective story about blackmail, murder, and augmented bodies. in particular a device that lets you control your emotions through the hormone levels in your blood -- and as ex-cop ruth often wonders, is that really something you need to make the right decision in the heat of the moment?<br /></blockquote>
  <b>THE PAPER MENAGERIE</b>
  <br />
  <blockquote>✎ <i>5.0 stars.</i><br /><b><i>but can you understand how much joy your existence brought me?</i></b><br /><br />the titular story that won several awards. about the magic of paper animals, and the pain of cultural assimilation. i’ll be honest: this one fucked me six ways to sunday. it reminded me so much of my grandmother, now long gone, telling me tales of where our family came from before the war destroyed her home.<br /></blockquote>
  <b>AN ADVANCED READERS’ PICTURE BOOK OF COMPARATIVE COGNITION</b>
  <br />
  <blockquote>✎ <i>3.0 stars.</i><br /><b><i>... the afterimages and last words of dead civilizations that have lost the struggle against entropy.</i></b><br /><br />a father reads a book to his child about the nature of thought, memory, and love. despite the hard science regarding interstellar radio waves, this felt very soothing and dreamy.<br /></blockquote>
  <b>THE WAVES</b>
  <br />
  <blockquote>✎ <i>3.5 stars.</i><br /><b><i>rebel. change is the only constant.</i></b><br /><br />how the origin stories and myths of our species get told over and over again, tweaked and twisted by immortality, while what it means to be human changes across the stretch of the galaxy. beautiful concept.<br /></blockquote>
  <b>MONO NO AWARE</b>
  <br />
  <blockquote>✎ <i>3.0 stars.</i><br /><b><i>understand that we are not defined by our individual loneliness, but by the web of relationships in which we’re enmeshed.</i></b><br /><br />this one is about what we sacrifice for the greater good. about how something that’s ingrained in us, taught to us by our family and our culture, can inspire that sacrifice many years later. the last japanese man in space finds a way to save humanity.<br /></blockquote>
  <b>ALL THE FLAVORS</b>
  <br />
  <blockquote>✎ <i>3.5 stars.</i><br /><b><i>if i didn’t know better, logan, i’d say you sound like a chinese american.</i></b><br /><br />this western, taking place in 1865, is about a girl (and eventually a whole city) befriending a group of chinese miners renting a room at her parents’ house. through her newfound friendship, she samples from chinese food, mythology, and games -- and shares some of their own culture, too.<br /></blockquote>
  <b>A BRIEF HISTORY OF THE TRANS-PACIFIC TUNNEL</b>
  <br />
  <blockquote>✎ <i>4.0 stars.</i><br /><b><i>... and these are the shackles that bound men whose voices were forever silenced, whose names were forgotten.</i></b><br /><br />a reimagining of history in which japan is one of the biggest world powers, ww2 never happened, and cheap asian laborers were used to dig a tunnel through the earth’s crust connecting asia and america. a story about making impossible choices and being changed forever because of what you went through. i haven’t seen any reviewers mention it yet, but this story reminded me in an eerie way of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burma_Railway" rel="nofollow noopener">burma railway.</a><br /></blockquote>
  <b>THE LITIGATION MASTER AND THE MONKEY KING</b>
  <br />
  <blockquote>✎ <i>4.0 stars.</i><br /><b><i>we’re all just ordinary men -- well, i’m an ordinary demon -- faced with extraordinary choices.</i></b><br /><br />a historical tale from the qinglong dynasty with a bit of myth. an elderly man with a clever tongue like that of a trickster, known for defending peasants in court, ends up being part of something he cannot bring his countrypeople and government to ever forget.</blockquote>
  <b>THE MAN WHO ENDED HISTORY: A DOCUMENTARY</b>
  <br />
  <blockquote>✎ <i>5.0 stars.</i><br /><b><i>the fact that we can never have complete, perfect knowledge does not absolve us of the moral duty to judge and to take a stand against evil.</i></b><br /><br />i don’t know how to rate or review this; i don’t know if i can. it raises so many legitimately good and current questions: those of perception and observation and the bias of history, of the ownership of tragedies, of what it means to commit the most terrible of war crimes. what kind of justice we owe to ourselves, to the victims, and to the perpetrators. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unit_731" rel="nofollow noopener">unit 731 was real, as were the atrocities committed there.</a></blockquote>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="6412359523249223257" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_348795842" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/348795842" />
    <a title="Maggie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222084-maggie"><img alt="Maggie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319666686p2/4222084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=i-ve-just-read-you-and-i-love-you">i-ve-just-read-you-and-i-love-you</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer348795842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15245302498147392720">Well, this short story made me cry more in 15 pages than any other book I've read this year -- except for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/370361.Patrick_Ness' title='Patrick Ness' rel='nofollow noopener'>Patrick Ness</a>'s gut punches masquerading as books. This story of the Chinese-American son of a mail order bride who learns of his otherness from cruel neighborhood kids and begins to resent the source of his difference, his mother, was heartbreaking, poignant, and familiar. It reminded me of all the times my brother and I would refuse to eat with chopsticks or speak Korean, how we demanded na</span>
  <span id="freeText15245302498147392720" style="display:none">Well, this short story made me cry more in 15 pages than any other book I've read this year -- except for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/370361.Patrick_Ness" title="Patrick Ness" rel="nofollow noopener">Patrick Ness</a>'s gut punches masquerading as books. This story of the Chinese-American son of a mail order bride who learns of his otherness from cruel neighborhood kids and begins to resent the source of his difference, his mother, was heartbreaking, poignant, and familiar. It reminded me of all the times my brother and I would refuse to eat with chopsticks or speak Korean, how we demanded nasty Lunchables instead of kimbap, the DELICIOUS Korean version of sushi that was packed in our lunches.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380380843i/737872.jpg" width="350" height="253" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When Jack demands that his mother speak only English, she says,<br><blockquote>“If I say ‘love,’ I feel here.” She pointed to her lips.<br>“If I say ‘ai,’ I feel here.” She put her hand over her heart.</blockquote>These two lines sum up why so many immigrants cling to their native tongue despite the protestations of their non-immigrant children.<br><br>Thanks to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/309479728" rel="nofollow noopener">Flannery</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/348705241" rel="nofollow noopener">Leanne</a> for bringing this story to my attention. It's definitely worth the few minutes it'll take to read. Just be sure to have tissues handy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15245302498147392720" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dr3V+e5D3iZuYhQ1Lv5o90d/NUG+sKyJaEy7Of/O1EeizZFfZkQgm6a1GSP3N298UdByAwEmmW/SG9IAdtkCeQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('b270YUTKll9V1VKrS0Xz+kqHF7prKHyV/iQzTxZVdZq7HrDHzM1o4p0CX72SjPRxXChQ+NS+SXNEc1p2n0KjpA==')})
  }

In The Merchant and the Alchemist\'s Gate, a portal th<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText4072411170960815142\" style=\"display:none\">An alternate cover edition for this book can be found here.\n\nThis much-anticipated second collection of stories is signature Ted Chiang, full of revelatory ideas and deeply sympathetic characters. In The Merchant and the Alchemist\'s Gate, a portal through time forces a fabric seller in ancient Baghdad to grapple with past mistakes and the temptation of second chances. In the epistolary Exhalation, an alien scientist makes a shocking discovery with ramifications not just for his own people, but for all of reality. And in The Lifecycle of Software Objects, a woman cares for an artificial intelligence over twenty years, elevating a faddish digital pet into what might be a true living being. Also included are two brand-new stories: Omphalos and Anxiety Is the Dizziness of Freedom.In this fantastical and elegant collection, Ted Chiang wrestles with the oldest questions on earth—What is the nature of the universe? What does it mean to be human?—and ones that no one else has even imagined. And, each in its own way, the stories prove that complex and thoughtful science fiction can rise to new heights of beauty, meaning, and compassion.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"4072411170960815142\" A deaf Native American girl wanders off into the desert and is found untouched in a den of rattlesnakes. A young boy copes with the death of his sister by angling for an unnaturally large trout in the creek where she drowned. An old woman rides her horse into a mountain snowstorm and sees a long-dead beloved dog. For the plainspoken men and women of these stories--fathers and daughters, sheriffs and veterinarians--small events trigger sudden shifts in which the ordinary becomes unfamiliar. A harmless comment about how to ride a horse changes the course of a relationship, a snakebite gives rise to hallucinations, and the hunt for a missing man reveals his uncanny resemblance to an actor. Half an Inch of Water tears through the fabric of the everyday to examine what lies beneath the surface of these lives. At the country\'s edge, on the Mexican border, Brownsville, Texas, is a town like many others. It is a place where people work hard to create better lives for their children, where people bear grudges against their neighbors, where love blossoms only to fade, and where the only real certainty is that life holds surprises. In his sparkling debut, Oscar Casares creates a cast of unforgettable characters confronting everyday possibilities and contradictions: Diego, an eleven-year-old whose job at a fireworks stand teaches him a lesson in defiance; Bony, a young man whose discovery of a monkey\'s head on his lawn drives a wedge between him and his parents; Lola, whose stolen bowling ball offers an unlikely chance for change. The achievement of Brownsville lies in its remarkably honest portrayal of these lives -- the lives of people whose dreams and yearnings and regrets are at once unique and universal. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16282441783333905175">Ken Liu (<a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://kenliu.name'>http://kenliu.name</a>) is an American author of speculative fiction. He has won the Nebula, Hugo, and World Fantasy awards, as well as top genre honors in Japan, Spain, and France, among other places.<br/><br/>Ken's debut novel, The Grace of Kings, is the first volume in a silkpunk epic fantasy series, The Dandelion Dynasty, in which engineers play the role of wizards. His debut collection, The Paper </span>
  <span id="freeText16282441783333905175" style="display:none">Ken Liu (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://kenliu.name">http://kenliu.name</a>) is an American author of speculative fiction. He has won the Nebula, Hugo, and World Fantasy awards, as well as top genre honors in Japan, Spain, and France, among other places.<br /><br />Ken's debut novel, The Grace of Kings, is the first volume in a silkpunk epic fantasy series, The Dandelion Dynasty, in which engineers play the role of wizards. His debut collection, The Paper Menagerie and Other Stories, has been published in more than a dozen languages. He also wrote the Star Wars novel, The Legends of Luke Skywalker.<br /><br />He has been involved in multiple media adaptations of his work. The most recent projects include “The Message,” under development by 21 Laps and FilmNation Entertainment; “Good Hunting,” adapted as an episode of Netflix's breakout adult animated series Love, Death + Robots; and AMC's Pantheon, which Craig Silverstein will executive produce, adapted from an interconnected series of short stories by Ken.<br /><br />Prior to becoming a full-time writer, Ken worked as a software engineer, corporate lawyer, and litigation consultant. Ken frequently speaks at conferences and universities on a variety of topics, including futurism, cryptocurrency, history of technology, bookmaking, the mathematics of origami, and other subjects of his expertise.<br /><br />Ken is also the translator for Liu Cixin's The Three-Body Problem, Hao Jingfang's Vagabonds, Chen Qiufan's Waste Tide, as well as the editor of Invisible Planets and Broken Stars, anthologies of contemporary Chinese science fiction.<br /><br />He lives with his family near Boston, Massachusetts.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16282441783333905175" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

Our minds managed to touch, if but briefly and imperfectly.<br /><br />Does that thought not make the universe seem just a bit kinder, a bit brighter, a bit warmer and more human?<br /><br />We live for such miracles.&rdquo;</span>
